Rural Life Miscellany 33

— Shao Shiping

Land Relations and Taxes in Sichuan (Continued)

However, there are many more dire situations. In Wanxian and other places, land leases are subject to one-sided contracts. Once farmers become tenants, they are bound by various contractual restrictions and are required to pay huge deposits. For every ten piculs of rent, a deposit of over one hundred yuan is required. If several families compete for the same piece of land, the deposit can increase infinitely. If the rent is slightly in arrears, the landlord can immediately terminate the lease and recruit another tenant. The tenant has to face lawsuits, imprisonment, beatings, and even torture and murder are not uncommon. In Lujiang, Jiang'an, and other places, rents are often arbitrarily increased, increasing by one-third within two years. The lives of tenant farmers naturally become increasingly miserable.

Land Tax and Levies

The high land tax and heavy levies in Sichuan are world-famous. Because the sustenance of more than 400,000 troops and the expenses of the government can only be taken from the people. Now let's look at a statistic.

Tax burden per mu of farmland in Sichuan (see Sweat and Blood, Volume 4, Issue 4)

Year 22 Survey: Zhangming 8.200 2.050, Guanghan 3.750 893, Qu County 4.000 1.000, Chengdu 2.560 640, Mianyang 2.030 508, Peng County 1.750 438, Neijiang 1.585 375, Ya'an 1.274 319, Guan County 1.085 271

The lightest land tax burden per mu (Guan County) is more than one yuan, and the heaviest (Zhangming) is more than eight yuan. The average is about one yuan and five jiao to four yuan. Compared to the productivity per mu of land in Sichuan, it is indeed very heavy. Even in the paddy field areas of Jiangnan, the land tax per mu rarely exceeds two yuan, but it is already high enough; how much more is it when it reaches more than eight yuan! Moreover, the land tax is increasing, and the burden on farmers is increasing year by year, which is an undeniable fact.

Changes in Land Tax and Percentage of Land Value in Sichuan Over the Years

(Survey by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute)

The above table tells us how fast the land tax is increasing! From the beginning of the Republic of China to the 22nd year of the Republic of China, in these 22 years, both paddy fields and dry land have increased by about one time, and in recent years they are still continuing to rise.

However, we cannot understand the suffering of farmers without explaining the pre-collection of land tax. Pre-collection of land tax is the specialty of the military and political authorities in Sichuan. In the beginning of the 21st year of the Republic of China, Chengdu pre-collected until the 28th year, Chongning until the 38th year, Xindu County until the 41st year, Guang'an for 12 years, Peng'an for 24 years, and other places had similar situations to varying degrees. Currently, many places have collected up to 80 or 90 years, or 60 or 70 years, and each county collects more than ten times a year, and at least four or five times. Farmers use all their produce to pay the land tax, and there is often a risk of insufficiency.

However, how does such a land tax affect the big landlords? We know that they are not greatly affected. First, the big landlords cannot be separated from politics, they are important figures in local politics. Second, even if we take a step back, because the military and political authorities rely on guns to collect land tax, they cannot do so without going through their hands, so it is a good opportunity for them to profit. Third, big landlords often do not live in the countryside, or are in other counties. Moreover, due to defense zone relations, there is nothing to be done about them. The authorities implement the method of "following the land to find grain," whoever cultivates the land must pay taxes. The most unlucky ones are the tenant farmers. Naturally, small landlords who are not involved in politics and middle and poor farmers who have no way to leave the area can only be exploited. In recent years, the decline of weak and powerless landlords and the rise of new landlords who participate in political activities are also due to this.

The year before last, after Chairman Chiang entered Sichuan, he spared no effort to improve Sichuan's administration. Therefore, Liu Xiang telegraphed the entire province, stipulating that the land tax should be collected once a year from March 1st of this year (24th year), but before the bandit suppression military affairs are over and the army is not yet reorganized, temporary military expenses three times the amount of tax may be attached. This is tantamount to saying that the land tax for four years must be collected in one year, but it cannot be used as a pre-collection. This is naturally much better than collecting more than ten times a year.

But what is the situation in various places after the implementation of the new policies? We may as well take facts to illustrate:

According to the Dagongbao on April 14th of last year, "The Sichuan armies are still taking advantage of the opportunity to exploit as much as possible during the period of food shortage. Xinjin County immediately levied grain tax. Qionglai also started collecting new grain, and added a learning fee of 7.5 jiao per tael, limited to be cleared by the end of May. Yuechi levied 900,000 yuan, limited to be paid by the end of April, but the grain tickets were even filled in with past dates, causing the county residents to escape to Chongqing to accuse Yang Sen. According to the same newspaper on March 13th, the 28th Army, under the guise of urgent military expenses, ordered the Guan County government to start collecting grain tax for two years on March 8th (that is, eight days after the promulgation of the new policy). The situation in northern Sichuan is even more pitiful. Let us read the petition of the people of northern Sichuan, Zhang Lan, etc., to Chairman Chiang: (see Dagongbao on March 26th of last year) Yang Sen, the 20th Army Commander, killed 12,000 shi of grain in Nanchong in February of the 23rd year under the name of supplying military food, and actually resold it, causing the savings of middle-class families to be exhausted. Recently, Yang Hancheng, the Brigade Commander of the army, again dispatched 2,000 shi of grain from Nanchong, limiting the time for payment, not knowing what it was for. The army commander has now ordered Nanchong to collect grain from March 1st (that is, the day of the new policy reform -- the author), at a rate of more than 57 yuan per tael. It is found that the annual tax of Nanchong is more than 9,500 taels, and according to the old practice, each tael should only collect 7 yuan, 9 jiao, 1 cent and 3 li a year, totaling no more than 67,000 yuan. This time, the tax is 57 yuan per tael, which is equivalent to collecting eight years of grain, totaling more than 530,000 yuan, and is limited to be cleared in one month, which is shocking..." The situation in northern Sichuan is roughly the same. Southern Sichuan is also the same, let's take Gulin as an example. Gulin was originally a remote place with barren land and poor people, and suffered from the oppression of warlords and corrupt officials. The people had long been unable to make ends meet. After the "Communists" infiltrated, the large army entered the county, requisitioning grain and looting property, resulting in "ten houses out of ten empty". Unexpectedly, as soon as the "Communists" retreated, the county government immediately announced the collection of four years of land tax and 80,000 yuan of opium tax (opium seedling fine). The people could no longer bear it. Therefore, a special telegram was sent to the provincial government, requesting that "an order be issued to stop it", otherwise, "please send troops to Gulin to slaughter all 300,000 people in the county together, which would be more enjoyable". They could no longer endure the piecemeal gouging. In short, as the Chengdu Provincial Association in southwestern Sichuan complained to Chairman Chiang, "Since the implementation of the unified tax, the garrison troops in various defense zones still do not understand the great righteousness. Taking advantage of this transitional period, they collude with the heads of the regiment to intensify the squeeze on our people, forcibly taking all kinds of exorbitant taxes. The suffering of our people is even greater than before." This is absolutely true. But when will the "transitional period" be extended to?

Moreover, the collection of land tax is very strict, and there are as many tax collection commissioners as there are carp crossing the river. The demands and harassment are unbearable. For example, the grain tax in Zizhong County has now been collected until the 60th year of the Republic of China, and the accumulated grain arrears over the years are also more than 20,000 yuan. The county government convened the heads of various rural regiments to discuss the results, and decided to hand over the grain team to collect the arrears with interest, supervised by the heads of the regiment, and pay it off in three installments, each installment lasting 20 days. Each grain ticket must add a "food fee" of 2 jiao, and one yuan for collecting grain. The first installment adds 1 jiao of interest, the second installment adds 1.5 jiao, and the third installment adds 2 jiao. If it is not paid off within these 60 days, it will be "dealt with according to the law". This situation is not only in Zizhong, and not only when collecting grain arrears, but also the same in the collection of grain tax in various counties.

Other miscellaneous taxes are also varied and numerous, such as the gun purchase fee for households and militia! The militia gun fee! The militia ammunition fee! The weir repair fee! The laziness tax (not planting opium)! All kinds of names are different in each county, and the statistics of the whole province are more than 2,000 kinds, breaking the record of all provinces. No wonder there is a cry of "Our Sichuan has suffered from exorbitant taxes for a long time. Officials squeeze and suck the marrow. The desires are difficult to fill. The people endure the pain and burden of ancestors. The sweat is dry and the blood is exhausted. In the past, it was called the Land of Abundance, but now it has become a ghost cave." (The End)

Page 7

Tokyo Incident Comes to an End, New Developments in Japanese Politics, Cabinet of National Unity to Appear Soon, Recruiting Talents to Clarify Politics, Military's Intentions Still Absolutely Respected 34

Regarding the selection of the leader of the successor cabinet in Tokyo, the attitude of key figures is extremely cautious. Recently, it is expected that Prince Saionji, the elder statesman, will make a significant reply. It is heard that the following points are special to the successor cabinet:

The full intentions of the military must be respected; High-minded and sincere talents must be recruited from all parties to create a cooperative cabinet of national unity; At the same time as the establishment of the talent cabinet, diplomacy, internal affairs, finance, economy, etc. will be renewed with the people; There must be the strength to implement confident policies to refresh people's minds and demonstrate the transformation of the times and its leap forward; In order to put an end to this crisis and thoroughly implement the purpose of purifying the army, the appointment of the Minister of the Army must be the focus; When requesting to join the cabinet, there is no need to avoid whether there is party affiliation, and political parties are not the first priority. The method of talent-basedism should be adopted as much as possible to show the clarity of the political arena.

After putting an end to this unprecedented and ominous incident, a clear successor cabinet will be organized and specific actions will begin. Once Prince Saionji comes to Kyoto to reply to the questions, the movements of various political parties, the interactions of senior officials, and various attitudes will be on the right track. The various situations in the political arena will reach the peak of tension. This is the general observation. (A dispatch from the Allied News Agency on the 1st)

The Tokyo government is paying attention to various situations in order to formulate comprehensive policies for dealing with the current situation. At 10:00 AM today, an extraordinary cabinet meeting was held in the palace to discuss various measures for the aftermath. For the sake of stabilizing the public, the government decided to continue following the policy stated by Prime Minister Okada and make a public announcement after the cabinet meeting. (A dispatch from the Allied News Agency on the 1st)

After holding the final cabinet meeting in the Ministry of the Imperial Household today, Prime Minister Okada and all the cabinet members visited the Emperor to confess their guilt and dismantled the cabinet's branch office in the Ministry of the Imperial Household. At 4:55 PM, Prime Minister Okada, without bodyguards, took a car alone to visit the residences of various princes and made a special confession, and then returned to a temporary private residence in the city. Other cabinet members also left the Imperial Palace, so the government agencies have returned to normal. (A dispatch from the Electric Communication Agency on the 1st)

Since the incident on the 26th, the government cabinet members who moved to the meeting room of the Ministry of the Imperial Household have withdrawn today. Prime Minister Okada and others will hold cabinet meetings at the Prime Minister's official residence in Nagatacho at 10:00 AM every day to deal with the current situation. (A dispatch from the Electric Communication Agency on the 1st)

Selection of Successor Cabinet Members, Still Quite a Few Twists and Turns 35

The rebel troops in Tokyo were completely subdued at 2:00 PM on the 29th, and the situation has come to an end. In view of the current situation, it is considered necessary to decide on the successor cabinet as soon as possible. Senior officials such as Prince Saionji are carefully considering it. However, after the fact that Prime Minister Okada, who was reported to have been killed during the suppression of the rebellion, is now actually alive was announced, a major impact occurred on the development of the political situation. However, Prime Minister Okada has submitted his resignation on the 28th, so the total resignation of the Okada Cabinet has been decided and will not give the situation a new change. Therefore, the political situation is still urgent, and the selection of the successor cabinet and the successor to the Minister of the Imperial Household is extremely urgent. At this time when the situation is complex and serious, it is still questionable whether the issue of the successor prime minister can be resolved quickly. In terms of objective circumstances, it is not easy to find a suitable person for the position of successor prime minister, and there seem to be quite a few twists and turns. As for the selection of the successor to the Minister of the Imperial Household, whether it will be decided before the formation of the cabinet is also related to the issue of the successor prime minister, so no decision has been made yet. The future is quite worthy of attention. (A dispatch from the Allied News Agency on the 1st)

Okitsu: Regarding the issue of the successor cabinet, senior officials are studying it. It is heard that Prince Saionji will come to Kyoto on the 2nd to reply to the questions. (A dispatch from the Allied News Agency on the 1st)

With the Tokyo incident resolved and the overall situation trending towards calm, the selection of the successor cabinet and the successor to the Minister of the Imperial Household is being carefully studied by elder statesmen and senior officials. It is believed that the duties of the Minister of the Imperial Household are important in assisting the Emperor in peacetime, and a decision should be made quickly. Currently, Prince Saionji and Minister of the Imperial Household Yuasa are discussing whether to invite a member of the imperial family to succeed to this position. This opinion seems to be quite powerful. As for the successor cabinet, Prince Saionji will reply to the questions and plans to listen to the opinions of senior officials, carefully consider the changes in the situation, and elect someone with popular support to organize a cooperative cabinet of national unity. The following figures are about to be nominated:

Baron Tatsuo Yamamoto, Count Keigo Kiyoura, Kurahei Yuasa, Baron Kiichiro Hiranuma, Duke Fumimaro Konoe, General Misao Kawai.

Uprising of Japanese Soldiers; Foreign Policy Unchanged; Not Expected to Endanger Pacific Peace; Japanese Ambassador Delivers Broadcast Speech in the US 45

Washington - Ambassador Saito of Japan delivered a broadcast speech last night, stating that the Tokyo incident would absolutely not disrupt the peace of the Pacific. He also denounced warmongers as a scourge of the nation, saying that if the Japanese government were indeed controlled by such individuals, it would be a great disaster for Japan. However, he asserted that the majority of military personnel do not harbor bellicose intentions, thus soldiers are beneficial to the country, but warmongers are detrimental. Japan's domestic and foreign policies will not change due to recent events. He concluded that although the incident was unfortunate, the rebels acted out of sincere patriotism, and it is regrettable that they were misled. Their motives seem to stem from fear that the government is controlled by financial cliques, leading to corruption, a mistaken notion not unique to Japanese youth, but also present in many other countries. The Strength of the Soviet Air Force, According to a French Military Expert; 2,800 Aircraft; 600 Stationed in the Far East 48

Paris - According to General Niesessel, a well-known French military expert, of the 2,800 aircraft, 70 squadrons are fighter planes and 80 squadrons are reconnaissance planes, totaling 1,400. General Niesessel stated that of these 2,800 aircraft, 600 are stationed in the Far East, leaving only 2,200 to cope with the situation in Europe. In the event of war, only fighter planes could be used in an emergency. The Soviet Union has approximately 500 fighter planes stationed in the Far East, and those in Europe can only fly within 6,000 miles, making them ineffective for targets in Poland, which is 5,000 miles away. General Niesessel also stated that the long-promoted Soviet paratrooper operations are nothing more than exaggeration. According to foreign experts who have witnessed their performances, they are completely useless behind enemy lines. General Niesessel concluded that the Soviet air force is an important military component, but it would be wishful thinking to believe that this air force could successfully engage Germany in war. (Guomin News Agency, 29th)

Border Conflict Incident; Outer Mongolia Responds to Manchukuo's Protest; Suggests Forming a Committee to Investigate the Truth 49

Moscow/Kulun News - On February 25th, the Foreign Minister of "Manchukuo" sent a memorandum to the Mongolian Premier and Foreign Minister Genden, raising the issue of the border between the two countries. In this memorandum, the "Manchukuo Government" accused Mongolian troops of continuously attacking "Manchukuo" territory south of Lake Bel, plundering the peaceful people and cattle in that area. At the same time, the "Manchukuo Government" protested the incident of February 12th, regarding which the Government of the Mongolian People's Republic had already announced the details in a protest to the "Manchukuo Government" on February 13th.

To rationalize this delayed protest, the "Manchukuo Government" claimed that the February 12th incident was the result of the Mongolian authorities illegally occupying Ulan Khuduk, a place allegedly belonging to "Manchukuo." The "Manchukuo Government" demanded that Mongolian troops immediately withdraw from this "forcibly occupied" territory and that similar incidents not occur again, otherwise, it would reserve the right to take free action.

At the same time, the "Manchukuo Government" continued to mention the necessity of establishing diplomatic relations and seeking peaceful resolutions to border disputes, claiming that the Mongolian proposal to organize a border committee was impractical. The "Manchukuo Government" declared that if Mongolia could propose a more effective and appropriate method, it would be willing to sincerely, impartially, and cooperatively discuss such a proposal. The Foreign Minister of "Manchukuo" requested to be informed of the views of the Mongolian People's Republic in the near future.

Outer Mongolia Responds - In response to this memorandum, the Mongolian Foreign Minister sent the following memorandum today: "I believe it is necessary to reiterate that the entire course of the conflict that occurred in Bulantsen, within the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic on February 12th, has been described in detail and accurately in my protest of February 13th, which unfortunately did not receive a response. I deeply regret that you have failed to meet our legitimate demands made in that protest, and instead, in your protest, you declare us to be illegal and demand that we withdraw from the "Manchukuo" territory allegedly occupied by our troops. The Government of the Mongolian Republic reiterates that our troops have never invaded the "Manchukuo" border, nor have they occupied its territory or plundered its peaceful people and cattle, and that all these incidents in fact occurred within the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic, as a result of your country's troops invading our border and attacking our border guards. The Government of the Mongolian People's Republic is deeply willing to maintain peaceful relations with all its neighbors and is prepared to make every effort to maintain peace and tranquility on its borders. The Government of the Mongolian People's Republic believes that such conflicts cannot be resolved due to the opposing interpretations of the events by both sides. In order to ascertain the truth, the Mongolian government proposes to immediately organize a mixed Manchu-Mongolian committee to investigate and report on the entire circumstances and causes of the February 12th incident, as well as other incidents that have occurred, providing reasons for mutual accusations. This committee will also be instructed to propose various methods to prevent similar conflicts from occurring in the future. If your country agrees, the Government of the Mongolian Republic is willing to immediately appoint representatives to participate in the mixed committee. The Government of the Mongolian Republic hopes that the "Manchukuo" government will fulfill the promise made in the February 25th memorandum, that is, to consider this proposal in a cooperative spirit and without bias, and to provide a satisfactory response promptly." (TASS, 29th)

Italian Troops Advance Victoriously in the North; Large Ethiopian Army Surrounded; Trapped in a Pincer Movement, in Dire Straits; Rome Celebrates Victory Enthusiastically 51

Rome - The strongest two Ethiopian armies on the northern front are in danger of being destroyed as a result of the Italian Third Army and the Eritrean Second Regiment's encirclement of the Tembien salient. According to Italian sources, the army led by Ethiopian Generals Kassa and Seyoum is now trapped in a pincer movement by Italian columns, facing either surrender or annihilation. The Ethiopian army realized yesterday that it was in a precarious situation and attempted to break through the Zemian Mountains, but the road was blocked by the Italian Third Army. According to a battle report from General Badoglio, commander of the Italian East African forces, the predicament of the two Ethiopian armies is worsening. The second major battle, which began at dawn on February 28th in the Tembien area, has reached its concluding phase. At the same time, the 9,000-foot-high Amba Aradam, considered the gateway to Ethiopia, has apparently been occupied by Italian troops without bloodshed. The entire nation of Italy rejoices. Mussolini has ordered flags to be flown everywhere on Sunday to celebrate. It is felt that this decisive victory will determine the outcome of the Ethiopian war, with Italy certain to prevail. (Reuters, 1st)

Rome - Today marks the 40th anniversary of the defeat of Italian troops at the Battle of Adwa in Ethiopia. US President Approves; Neutrality Act Extension; Prohibits Loans to Belligerents; New Concrete Step to Maintain Neutrality 53

Washington - The US President today approved the bill passed by both houses of Congress last week to extend the Neutrality Act to May 1, 1937. This plan aims to ensure US neutrality in the event of a war in Europe, prohibits lending to belligerents, and enables the President to declare a ban on the shipment of arms and ammunition to belligerents and to prohibit US travelers from traveling on belligerent ships in the event of war. No warships belonging to belligerents are allowed to enter US ports. According to a statement issued by President Roosevelt, the new Neutrality Act's prohibition of lending to belligerents is a new and concrete step towards maintaining US neutrality. Under the original law, the shipment of arms to both Italy and Ethiopia was prohibited. He also stated that he has now issued a new proclamation to meet the needs of the new law and that the neutrality policy initially announced by him and Secretary of State Hull will remain effective. President Roosevelt concluded by asking that trade with belligerents be limited to no more than peacetime levels. (Reuters, 29th)

Washington - President Roosevelt has signed the new Neutrality Act, extending the existing Neutrality Act's term of validity by 14 months, that is, until May 1, 1937. The various clauses contained in the existing Neutrality Act, whether temporary or permanent in nature, are preserved and supplemented with new clauses, which are explained separately below:

Temporary Clauses: The export of arms is prohibited to belligerents or neutral countries acting on behalf of belligerents. This clause remains in effect.

Permanent Clauses: Stipulate that (A) merchants manufacturing and selling arms must apply for registration; (B) foreign submarines may not use US seaports as a base; (C) the President may, at his discretion, prohibit US citizens from boarding armed merchant ships of belligerents. These clauses remain in effect.

New Clauses: (A) Prohibits long-term and short-term loans to belligerents, but the President may approve short-term loans of a commercial nature to belligerents, as is customary; (B) The arms embargo does not apply to Latin American countries if they are attacked by countries outside of the Americas. However, the arms embargo will still apply if Latin American countries form an alliance with countries outside of the Americas during a war in the Western Hemisphere. (Havas, 29th)

Former British Prime Minister Lloyd George; Expresses Views on National Defense; Supports the Collective Security System; East Coast Easily Attacked by Enemy Forces; Naval Circles Advocate for More Anti-Aircraft Stations 54

London - Former Prime Minister Lloyd George, leader of the opposition Liberal Party, recently gave a speech on the issue of British national defense, stating, "The Liberal Party will study the government's white paper on rearmament (scheduled to be released next Wednesday)." He also stated, "The government's proposed approach, advocating that Britain's air force be on par with the air force of the most powerful country, is not sufficient to guarantee our country's security. The only hope for avoiding air warfare is to make it clear to all future aggressors that if our country is attacked, not only will our country rise up in self-defense, but also the power of the entire League of Nations will come to our aid. This force is unbreakable and cannot be defended against by any country in the world. Therefore, for Britain's sake, it should not isolate itself, but must cooperate with the League of Nations. This is why our party fully accepts the policy adopted by the League of Nations without reservation." (Havas, 29th)

London - According to information from this newspaper's reporter, naval circles in Britain are now extremely concerned about the eastern coast being close to the continent, making it vulnerable to enemy attacks in the event of a conflict. Conservative MP Sir Sothern mentioned this on the 13th of this month in the House of Commons, stating, "If the enemy launches aerial bombardments, the southeastern ports will bear the brunt, and they should be strictly defended." In light of this, naval circles have planned to build multiple anti-aircraft stations along the eastern coast, equipped with aircraft detection devices, so that the location of enemy aircraft formations can be detected upon hearing their approach. On the other hand, the western coast is not only farther from the continent, but even if enemy aircraft were to cross the border, the rumbling of their engines would be heard before they reached their destination, making it less vulnerable to enemy attacks. (Havas, 29th)

London - The government plans to add a Minister without Portfolio who will be specifically responsible for coordinating national defense affairs. This newspaper's reporter has learned that one of the main tasks of this minister will be to reconcile the views of the Navy and the Air Force. The Navy believes that although air attacks are to be feared, they will not endanger the Navy. Therefore, it advocates that the rearmament plan should focus on the Navy. The Air Force, on the other hand, believes that in future wars, the Air Force will be able to decisively defeat battleships, and therefore demands that air force armaments be expanded with all resources. With these two opposing views, there is a need for reconciliation. (Havas, 29th)

Naval Qualitative Restrictions; Britain and Germany Negotiating Bilateral Agreement; To Supplement the Quantitative Restriction Treaty; Negotiations to Begin in London 56

London - Regarding the issue of Britain and Germany concluding a separate naval agreement outside of the Naval Conference, German Chancellor Hitler has authorized the German Ambassador to the UK, Herr von Hoesch, to begin negotiations with the British government in order to establish a bilateral qualitative restriction agreement to supplement the agreement concluded last June. It is expected that Ambassador von Hoesch will notify the British government of these instructions tomorrow. (Havas, 1st)

London - German Chancellor Hitler has agreed to begin negotiations in London to conclude a bilateral naval qualitative restriction treaty between Britain and Germany to supplement the existing naval quantitative restriction treaty between the two countries. The German Embassy in London has received these instructions in response to the proposal made by British Foreign Secretary Eden to the German Ambassador to the UK, Dr. Hoesch, that if the London Naval Conference can conclude a naval treaty, Britain and Germany should sign a bilateral treaty identical to that treaty. This procedure was initially proposed by France to dispel French objections to signing a comprehensive treaty including Germany, thereby avoiding the appearance of undermining the Treaty of Versailles. The only difference between this procedure and a comprehensive treaty including Germany is that, under the bilateral treaty, Germany will only notify Britain of its shipbuilding program, and Germany will only receive Britain's shipbuilding program, and not those of all the signatory countries. (Reuters, 1st)

Heading Up the Amazon River: French Youth Will Explore Inhabited South American Savage Tribes 64

Paris - Three French young explorers have formed an expedition team and will soon depart from here to explore the upper reaches of the Amazon River in South America. The team leader, Florene, is an experienced explorer who previously ventured deep into the Amazon River basin and is familiar with the customs and conditions there. He recently gave a speech here, explaining the purpose of this trip and detailing the history of Amazon exploration, from beginning to end, without omission. He stated that the team's planned route is to disembark at a port on the Pacific Ocean, then travel by small boat through the wilderness, down the Mapo River, and then up the Amazon River to the great waterfall near the Santiago River. Above that point is the territory of the uncivilized Jivaro people. The exploration will begin there. The purpose of our exploration is to investigate the geography and geology of the area, and to study the indigenous peoples and their customs. As far as I know, the vast forests of central South America have never been developed. The inhabitants are all savage tribes, and the Jivaro are the fiercest and most difficult to approach. Their hatred of civilization is also the greatest. In the early 17th century, when the Spanish invaded their territory from Peru, they established five cities for Spanish residents, but all were destroyed by the Jivaro, and over five thousand Spanish residents were killed. Afterwards, this area returned to its original state. These people live in the forests, dwell in tribes, and always carry weapons with them. They do not associate with white or red people. They destroy any small paths in the forest that could lead to their homes. Fighting is commonplace. Grudges often accumulate between clans, leading to tribal warfare. The victors not only cut off the heads of the defeated for pleasure, but they also carefully preserve these heads, making them into dried wax. The method is to first dig out all the bones and flesh from the skull, and then fill it with hot stones. The outer muscles contract when heated, so a large skull shrinks to the size of an apple after this process. However, the face of the deceased, including the beard and eyebrows, is fully visible and does not change. This type of dried wax is called a "Tsantsas." Any adult man who does not have a Tsantsas cannot marry for life. This custom is truly cruel. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

London Chinese Art Exhibition to Close Tomorrow, Over 200,000 Visitors in Three Months 65

London - The London Chinese Art Exhibition at Burlington House is about to close (March 3rd). As a result, the number of visitors has increased in recent days. It is expected that the total number of 340,000 visitors to the French Exhibition will easily be surpassed. After the exhibition closes, packing and storage will begin immediately, working day and night, as the treasures must be returned to their original owners around the world within just three weeks. It is expected that they will not be transported back to China by British cruisers. However, they will certainly be escorted by warships. Some American enthusiasts wanted to transport the treasures to New York for exhibition, but this was not successful because the U.S. government could not provide the necessary naval transport ships. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

— Jin Dui

19. Cotton Industry of Jinghui Canal in Shaanxi

The Shaanxi Provincial Construction Department has been working on the testing, domestication, and breeding of seedless cotton for a long time, and the results are satisfactory. The department has promoted the establishment of Yanghua Production and Sales Cooperatives in the Jinghui Canal area of the province. The scope of the cooperative extends from Yongle Town in Jingyang in the west to Gaofeng Village in Gaoling County in the east, bounded by the Zhongbai Canal in the north and the border between Yongle Town and Houzitou in the south. The area is ten li long from east to west and five li from north to south. Ten villages within this area have joined the cooperative, half belonging to Jingyang and half to Gaoling. The cotton planted is pure seedless cotton, with long fibers and a clean color. The planting is regulated with row spacing of two and a half feet and plant spacing of one foot. Adjustments can be made based on soil fertility. The total cotton field area is over 4,452 mu, yielding over 110,000 jin of ginned cotton. Each time the cotton is harvested, the cooperative divides the cotton into grades, inspects for dryness and warmth, weighs it, and examines it for purity. Then, it is weighed and registered, and a cotton receipt is issued to decide whether to transport the cotton directly for sale outside the area, in order to avoid exploitation by cotton merchants and to receive government tax exemptions and transportation subsidies. The cotton is transported by a transportation company from the origin to Jiaokou, then loaded onto ships at Jiaokou and transported to Tongguan. The average freight cost for each dan (two bales) of cotton is four yuan and fifty cents. From Tongguan, it is loaded onto trains and transported to Shanghai. The freight cost for each dan (100 jin) is two yuan and seventy cents. After the cotton is transported to Shanghai, the average price is over forty yuan per dan (100 jin). However, superior cotton is often classified as inferior and cannot be sold outside the area, and must be sold to nearby cotton shops at a low price. This is the business situation of the Yongle District Guaranteed Liability Cotton Production and Sales Cooperative in the Jinghui Canal.

Page 9

Overseas Chinese After the Establishment of Consulate in Vietnam 83

Hanoi Correspondence - Consul Xu and Consul Zhong Strive for Equal Treatment, All Overseas Chinese Express Their Support

There are 500,000 of our compatriots living in Vietnam, over 400,000 in Saigon and the six provinces of Cambodia, and over 40,000 in Tonkin, all engaged in industry and commerce (especially workers). Due to our country's weakness, diplomacy has been virtually non-existent. Therefore, overseas Chinese are governed by the French as equals with the Vietnamese, and the legal treatment they receive is sometimes not even as good as that of the Vietnamese. Those who have lived in or passed through Vietnam for a long time are well aware of this. After lengthy discussions between the Chinese diplomatic authorities, the Sino-Vietnamese Treaty was renewed last year, and our country began to send Consuls to Saigon and Hanoi in accordance with the Treaty. From then on, overseas Chinese in Vietnam were able to see the dignity of Chinese officials. This is why overseas Chinese in Vietnam were overjoyed. When Consul-General Xu Nianceng and Consul Zhong Zhenjun arrived in Hanoi via Haiphong, tens of thousands of overseas Chinese lined the streets to welcome them. When the consulate was opened, overseas Chinese from thousands of miles away rushed to participate, recalling the past and weeping bitterly. Because overseas Chinese are far from their homeland and have suffered greatly from unequal treatment, they are filled with a deep longing for their homeland, and their joy turns to sorrow.

Most of the overseas Chinese in Vietnam are Cantonese, with the Fujianese accounting for 20%. Recently, due to the economic downturn, the number of overseas Chinese has gradually decreased. Even in Haiphong, the population has decreased from 15,000 to over 9,000. As for overseas Chinese education, except for the children of merchants with considerable assets, there are few opportunities for education, and education is subject to much interference from the French, making it impossible to develop. Therefore, the knowledge of the overseas Chinese community is extremely low, which is a source of worry for knowledgeable overseas Chinese, but there is nothing they can do. This is why the overseas Chinese in Vietnam have a particularly strong concern for their homeland and participate in aiding the revolution particularly actively. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's revolution in South China relied on Haiphong as a base, as it had the economic support of the overseas Chinese in Vietnam.

The French have always implemented a "Bang" system to govern overseas Chinese. The "Bangs" are divided by province, or even by prefecture or language. The French allow each "Bang" to elect a "Bang" leader to represent the overseas Chinese. However, this "representation" only represents the French in collecting taxes from the overseas Chinese to facilitate their control. The French policy is designed to divide the overseas Chinese. Therefore, ignorant overseas Chinese never think about uniting, and factions are often divided and disagree. Among the "Bang" leaders, there are some enthusiastic people with a deep sense of justice who care about the dignity of the country, but there are also many greedy and ignorant people who are willing to be used by foreigners to exploit their compatriots. This unfortunate situation has lasted for decades without change. Since the establishment of the consulate, they have unanimously expressed their support under the idea of the nation, and handed over the command of the overseas Chinese to the consulate. This must be regarded as a fortunate event for the overseas Chinese. However, the French authorities in Vietnam believe that this is detrimental to their ruling power and refuse to abolish it. Consul Xu and Consul Zhong have argued on the basis of reason, and this matter is still in progress. The reporter met with Consul Zhong yesterday and asked about this matter. Consul Zhong said that he is continuing negotiations and will never fail to live up to the expectations of the government and the overseas Chinese, and is willing to make any sacrifices. The reporter shook hands with him respectfully to express his gratitude.

The consulate was established on December 18th last year. The work of the consulate is quite busy. The French have a very harsh "Overpass Permit Tax" for overseas Chinese. This permit, which overseas Chinese call "Humanity Paper" (used for traveling within Vietnam), must be renewed every fifteen days, and each renewal costs one Vietnamese dollar. As a result of negotiations, the French authorities have ordered its cancellation. According to Consul Zhong, negotiations are underway regarding the legal status of overseas Chinese, with the aim of obtaining the same treatment as British, American, and Japanese overseas residents. This move has gained the sincere sympathy of the overseas Chinese. In short, the overseas Chinese, who have suffered greatly, have had their eyes and ears refreshed since the opening of the consulate. (February 12th)

Secret Organization Discovered in Anhai, Quanzhou 84

Two Key Criminals Captured by Garrison Troops, Zhang Xiongnan Also Said to Have Been Used for Information

Xiamen Correspondence: In recent months, there have been many rumors in Xiamen and southern Fujian. According to a public announcement in Quanzhou on the 28th, in recent months, Japanese ronin have infiltrated the counties of Jinjiang, Nan'an, Hui'an, and Yongchun, evading taxes to smuggle goods, selling military supplies, colluding with unscrupulous merchants and traitors, either organizing smuggling agencies or secretly forming parties, and engaging in all kinds of illegal activities. On the night of the 23rd, troops stationed in Quanzhou cracked down on a large-scale smuggling agency in Shishi. On the night of the 26th, the garrison troops of the 52nd Regiment of the 9th Division in Anhai also cracked down on an organization called the "Youth Righteous Knights General Alliance" in Jinglin Township and captured two key criminals. Earlier, Zhu Xietuan, Battalion Commander of the 52nd Regiment of the 9th Division stationed in Anhai, received a report stating that suspicious foreigners were active in the market towns and villages under the jurisdiction of the Second District. He immediately sent his adjutant, Li Yuanchen, with thirty soldiers and two policemen from the Second District as guides, and rushed there on the evening of the 26th. When they approached Jinglin Township, they saw flickering lights and loud voices, as if they were aware of something. After a while, the troops were surrounded by the crowd in the dark. Li ordered platoon leader Duan Zigui to lead several soldiers to break through bravely and chase the bandits into a house. They fought fiercely with the bandits for several minutes. Duan was shot in the right chest and could not hold on. Then the troops rushed to surround the house, fought hand-to-hand and entered the house, capturing two people. One was Xu Xi, over 20 years old, who was seriously injured with a gunshot wound in his left leg, and the other was Su Lun, also over 20 years old. Both were dressed in black. A symbol with the number 0023 was found on Xu, with the words "Leader of the Youth Righteous Knights General Alliance." A pistol, 61 bullets, 3 hand grenades, and 7 ledgers of selling firearms and bullets were also found in the house. It was already 3:00 AM on the morning of the 27th. They were taken to Quanzhou for interrogation. Xu could not speak because of two bullets in his left leg. They arrived in Quanzhou on the evening of the 27th. After Su Lun was interrogated by the 52nd Regiment headquarters, he confessed that Xu Xi was selling firearms. He was then transferred to the Third District Pacification Headquarters. Xu died in a rickshaw on the way to Dongjie. Su was imprisoned and will continue to be interrogated.

Rumors have been rife in recent days in Nan'an Wharf and Yongchun that Chen Weijin has secretly returned to the wharf and has entered Dehua to conspire with the remnants of Zhang Xiongnan's troops (Zhang's troops recently defected during the re-enrollment). It is also said that Chen had discussed matters with Zhang in a certain place before returning (Chen fled last year and both lived in the capital of a certain country, Zhang recently returned to Hong Kong). Zhang Chengfu's troops of over 300 men under Zhang are now in the Annan Yongde border area, wantonly killing and looting for supplies. The 26th Brigade of the 9th Division is suppressing them under the personal command of Brigade Commander Xie Fu. According to a public announcement by the Quanzhou Pacification Department on the 28th, the bandits have suffered over 100 deaths. It is also reported that the bandits are showing signs of fleeing to the Xianyou border. The 9th Division has ordered the 49th Regiment in Xianyou to intercept them. Also, the bandit troops of Zhang Kewu have recently fled to Yunxi. It has been verified that Zhang Kewu's troops are also under Zhang Xiongnan. (March 1st)

New Regulations for Overseas Chinese Entering Nanyang 85

New Special and Harsh Regulations Intended to Restrict Overseas Chinese Entry

Xiamen Correspondence: Most of the overseas Chinese in the British, Dutch, French, and American territories of the Nanyang Islands are from southern Fujian. Every year, overseas Chinese from various territories of Nanyang returning to Fujian and those leaving Fujian for overseas use Xiamen as a port of departure and arrival. Therefore, there are over 80 ships sailing between Xiamen and various ports in Nanyang, the largest being 10,000 tons and the smallest 4,000 tons. On average, 7,000 people leave each month, and the number of arrivals is sometimes equal, but mostly exceeds the number of departures. Among them, the most go to the Dutch territories, followed by the British territories. However, the British, Dutch, American, and French territories have extremely strict restrictions on the entry of overseas Chinese. The Dutch and American territories are particularly strict. Recently, the Dutch territories have issued new regulations. Any overseas Chinese traveling with family members to Dairi, Batavia, Surabaya, Semarang, Julang, Kota, Sumatra, Bandung, and Wending in the Dutch territories must carry a marriage certificate and a certificate from the local Baojia chief, stamped by the county government, before they are allowed to go ashore. They must also pay 150 Dutch guilders per person to the local government as a guarantee deposit. If the investigation proves true, it can be returned within six months; otherwise, it will be confiscated and they will be deported. If the husband is in the Dutch territories and the wife is going there, or if they are taking their children with them, they must also pay 150 Dutch guilders per person and submit a marriage certificate. It has been verified that many overseas residents have been repatriated or deported due to incomplete procedures because they were not aware of the above new regulations. Also, the American Philippines has recently banned the entry of new overseas Chinese. Only old overseas Chinese who have a residence permit (commonly known as "Big Character") in the Philippines and are returning from their home country are allowed to return. If the old overseas Chinese own a store as the owner, their wives, mothers, and children may be granted entry permits. If they are workers, their families are not allowed. New immigrants must have a guarantee deposit of 1,000 US dollars, and a residence permit fee of 10 US dollars. Old overseas Chinese must pay an import tax of 8 US dollars and a residence permit fee of 10 US dollars. Also, the Dutch landing fee of 150 Dutch guilders (equivalent to 339 national currency) can be refunded if they leave the country within six months; otherwise, it will not be returned. The British Malaya import tax is 5 Singapore dollars (equivalent to 9.6 national currency), which can be refunded if they reside within one week. French Vietnam requires a head tax of 35 Annamese dollars (equivalent to 77 national currency), which cannot be refunded. Siam has an import license fee of 100 baht, a residence fee of 15 baht, and there are also unnamed national customs fees. It can be refunded if they leave the country within one year. As for the outbound ship ticket prices, taking third class as an example, it is 80 yuan to British Singapore, 90 yuan to Rangoon, 40 yuan to the American Philippines, and 66 yuan to Dutch Surabaya, and 81 yuan to Sabang. Also, the national passport fee issued by the Public Security Bureau is 4.6 yuan, and the signing fee at the Xiamen Consulate of the British, Dutch, and French territories is 12 yuan, and 4 yuan to Japan. Based on the above expenses, a single overseas Chinese cannot depart without substantial capital. The governments of the various Nanyang territories, in addition to using complicated legal procedures to make overseas Chinese fearful, also impose such heavy financial burdens, restricting them economically. The purpose is to restrict the entry of overseas Chinese. In fact, overseas Chinese will continue to go abroad as long as the Nanyang economy improves slightly, shoulder to shoulder, because the Fujian economy is declining and there is no employment to be found, so they have no choice but to go abroad to find new opportunities. (March 1st)

Rampant Bandits on the Fujian-Guangdong Border —Guangdong Army Deploys Troops to Vigorously Suppress— 86

Shantou Correspondence: Since the Chaozhou-Meizhou garrison made efforts last year to clear the countryside, implement Baojia (community policing), and suppress remaining bandits, the remnants in Raoping Phoenix Mountain, Chaoyang Nanshan, Fengshun Baxiang Mountain, Jieyang Beishan, Chao'an Sangpu Mountain, Chenghai Qinglan Cave, and other places have been completely unable to gain a foothold. Consequently, they have fled into the major mountains on the Fujian-Guangdong border, such as Pinghe Xianghu Mountain, Zhao'an Shangxiazhai, Lianhua Mountain, Yongding Yuantou Mountain, and other locations, which have become their final lairs. In places like Zhao'an Si Du, no fewer than twenty or thirty Baojia chiefs, grain collectors, and public officials in charge of donations have been oppressed and killed by bandits. No fewer than two or three hundred innocent people have been kidnapped and ransomed. Fifty or sixty have been robbed and killed. It is reported that the bandits operate in groups of thirty to fifty, openly setting fire to villages and towns during the day. As a result, villages like Taiping, Qicai, and Chezai Xu have been looted and burned, with more than ten villages being completely destroyed. The main force of the bandits is entrenched in several places, including Beizhe and Pingshui. The bandit leader, surnamed Zhou, is from Qiongshan County, Guangdong Province. He previously occupied the Sanping small mountain town area on the border of Nan靖, Hexi, and Zhangpu counties. Around July of last year, Zhou, acting on a false order, sneaked into Chizhu坪 in Zhao'an County, gathering the remnants of Yu Dingen, Yu Qitou, and Yu Hongmao from Raoping Phoenix Mountain. He proclaimed himself the "Political Commissar of the Red Army of Pseudo-Zhao (Zhao'an), Yun (Yunxiao), and He (Pinghe)," and reorganized the bandit gangs into the "Pseudo-Zhao'an Battalion," "Pinghe Battalion," and "Yunxiao Battalion." Because the terrain of Chizhu坪 was not as dangerous as that of Pingshui, in October, he moved the pseudo-general headquarters to Pingshui, specializing in harassing the Guangdong border. Later, the Guangdong Army's Zeng Youren Brigade stationed in Raoping County advanced to suppress Shangxiazhai. The bandit leader Yu Dingen was shot and killed. Zhou then appointed Chen Tingxiong as the pseudo-Yunxiao battalion commander, reorganizing the three hundred-odd bandits into a basic bandit army and forcing the villagers in the Beizhe and Pingshui areas to join the bandit party. Those who refused were robbed and killed. The bandit gangs of Yu Qitou and Yu Hongmao (who died on the Fen Shuiguan Ridge) are mostly composed of villagers from Raoping and Huanggang counties. They are now looting and kidnapping in Baxian, forty or fifty li away from Huanggang County. The Yu Qitou bandits are particularly fierce, having fought against the suppressing army several times. According to investigation, the strength of these gangs is as follows: Chen Tingxiong's command has 240 rifles, 4 submachine guns, 1 automatic rifle, and 26 Mauser pistols. Yu Qitou's command has 180 rifles and 24 Mauser pistols. However, both bandit gangs are severely short of ammunition. The Huang Renhuan Division stationed in Meixian is now additionally deploying the Chen Shuyiao Regiment to Dapu, to work with the Zeng Dayu, Chen Shaowu, and Ye Weihao regiments to strictly defend the Rao-Pu border. East Zone Commissioner Li Hanhun will inspect the Chaozhou-Meizhou-Fujian-Jiangxi border after Chief of Staff Li Yukun returns to Shantou from the province, to ensure vigorous suppression. (24th)

Overview of the Capital Telephone Bureau 87

Total of Four Branches and 7,300 Numbers Installed

Nanjing Communication: Automatic telephones in Nanjing began in July of the 19th year of the Republic. Appropriately after the establishment of the capital, government agencies were set up everywhere, and commerce flourished, leading to a sharp increase in users. At that time, the main bureau installed 3,000 numbers, the Gulou branch 1,000 numbers, and the Xiaguan branch 1,000 numbers, for a total of 5,000 numbers. By the 23rd year of the Republic, the capacity was full. It was decided that year, with the approval of the Ministry of Communications, to establish the South Branch in the old Jiangning County government office in the south of the city, adding 1,800 numbers. The North Branch (Gulou) was also expanded by 500 numbers at the same time, for a total of 7,300 numbers. It was originally scheduled to be operational last winter, but due to delays in delivery by the automatic telephone company, the new equipment for the North and South branches was only installed and put into operation last month. According to the person in charge of the bureau, the new equipment can temporarily cope with new users. In addition, the bureau has also established a branch in Shushan Town (the new site of the Jiangning County government), installing a 50-line magneto-type small exchange switchboard, which has already started construction and will soon be completed.

In terms of long-distance telephones, the Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Wuhu, Shanghai-Hangzhou, Bengbu, and Jiangbei lines operated by the ministry have long been connected. In addition, long-distance telephone lines operated by Jiangsu Province in Jiangning, Jurong, Lishui, Liyang, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Wujin, Yutan, Yixing, and other nine counties, as well as long-distance telephone lines operated by Zhejiang Province, can all be connected. Furthermore, long-distance telephone lines to Ping, Tianjin, Hunan, Hubei, Shandong, Jiangxi, and other provinces operated by the ministry will also be connected soon. As for the rest of Jiangsu Province, with the exception of the nine counties mentioned above, most other counties have already installed long-distance telephone lines. Because these are managed by the Provincial Department of Construction, they conflict with those managed by the ministry, forming a kind of opposition within the same system. Whether from the perspective of the business itself or the organizational system, it is extremely uneconomical and unreasonable, and it seems necessary to adjust it.

The telephone machinery room is located on the third floor of the bureau and is divided into six parts: the first and second line switches, the first to third selectors, and the terminator. The first line switch has 50 numbers as a group. Among these 50 numbers, only 10 can be connected at the same time. The second line switch has 60 numbers as a group, and 10 can be connected at the same time. When we dial the dial, we often hear a buzzing sound (busy signal), which indicates that someone is already on the line. The first selector has ten grids in both vertical and horizontal directions, and jumps according to the number we dial. For example, if we dial the number 4, it will jump vertically to the fourth grid, and then horizontally to the empty switch, connecting the second and third selectors. If the horizontal jump is in the eighth grid, it means that the first seven lines have already been occupied. Each selector only manages one number. Finally, the terminator specializes in managing the last two numbers. Usually, when we call a telephone, we must go through these six parts, from the first line switch to the terminator, relying on the operation of the machine, without manual labor, being able to automatically connect. It is truly an extremely ingenious thing.

The first digit of the telephone number represents the area. The "2" prefix belongs to the city center, where the main bureau is located. The Gulou area in the north of the city is "3," Xiaguan is "4," and after the establishment of the South Branch, the Zhonghua Gate area in the south of the city has been changed to "5" across the board.

When we use the telephone, we often encounter obstacles because the circuit is occupied, which has become a common phenomenon. This is very inappropriate. According to the person in charge of the bureau, according to regulations, the maximum percentage of calls that cannot be connected at the same time should be 20%, but the bureau has exceeded 70%. In other words, out of 100 telephones, at most 30 can be connected. In this way, it has to be said that there is a major flaw in the mission of the telephone itself.

The bureau was originally founded in the 26th year of the Guangxu reign of the late Qing Dynasty by the Viceroy of Liangjiang. At that time, it was a magneto type, with only 16 numbers, all occupied by important government agencies. In the 30th year of Guangxu, it was transferred to the Office of Military Training and began to open to merchants, but there were only 60-odd users. In the 3rd year of Xuantong, it was transferred to the Finance Public Office, and there were still only about 100 users. In the 2nd year of the Republic, it was taken over by the German Siemens company. In the 3rd year of the Republic, the Ministry of Communications took over the management and still used the magneto type. In the 9th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Communications decided to switch to the common battery type, purchasing the Western Electric Company's No. 1A exchange switchboard. At the same time, two branches were established in Xiaguan and Pukou. The city bureau installed a common battery type exchange with a capacity of 2,000 numbers, and Xiaguan installed a common battery type exchange with a capacity of 800 numbers. Pukou also installed a magneto type exchange with 100 numbers, laying underwater cables across the river. This was completed in the 11th year of the Republic. At this time, the number of users had increased to over 600. In the 14th year of the Republic, the Puzhen branch was opened. In the 15th year of the Republic, the Shanghai-Nanjing long-distance telephone was connected. By the first half of the 19th year of the Republic, the city had installed 2,000 numbers, Xiaguan 500 numbers, Pukou 70-odd numbers, and Puzhen 30-odd numbers. In July of that year, the world's prevailing automatic telephones were installed. In the 23rd year of the Republic, the Puzhen branch was abolished. In the 24th year of the Republic, the Pukou branch was also abolished, both merged into the Xiaguan branch. The above is a general overview of the bureau's past situation. In the early days of the bureau's establishment 36 years ago, there were only 16 telephones. After continuous improvements, it has now increased to 7,300 numbers. According to recent trends, it is still in short supply, and it will still need to be expanded soon. The future is limitless. In terms of the bureau's income and expenditure, it can collect more than 43,000 yuan in monthly rental fees and more than 5,000 yuan in machine deposit fees, for a total of more than 48,000 yuan. Recurring expenses include more than 13,000 yuan for employee salaries and 10,000 yuan for maintenance and office expenses, for a total of more than 23,000 yuan. After the automatic machine was converted, the price was more than 730,000 US dollars. The price of the new automatic machine for the South Branch was more than 142,000 US dollars. It is estimated that expanding the lines, replacing the new machines, purchasing the land, and building the bureau building cost more than 2.6 million yuan. Since the Ministry of Communications adopted the method of unified collection and payment, the bureau's income has been turned over to the ministry every month, and recurring expenses and machine price repayments are also allocated by the Ministry of Communications.

Spring Silkworm Seed Increase Doubles

Since the sales of foreign cloth were active and silk prices rose last year, the price of dried orchid also rose accordingly. It is expected that the number of cocoons produced will also increase by one times compared to last year, so silk factories need not worry about raw materials. Yangzhou 92

Resolution of the Official Wasteland Planting Mulberry Problem

The Provincial Silkworm Seed Manufacturing Institute previously requested the province to allocate official wasteland near Dapaotai in Aoyu Street Township and Laohushan in Fenghuang Town to plant mulberry trees, which caused problems. The Department of Construction specially sent commissioner Zhang Lunquan, the Department of Finance sent commissioner Liu Shifu, and the Jiangdu County Government also sent member Meng Zicai. On the afternoon of the 28th, they convened a meeting at the original silkworm manufacturing institute to discuss and decide on the method with the relevant district township Bao chiefs from the first and fourth districts, as well as the institute's director, Gu Yiting, and others. The decisions were as follows: For the official wasteland near Dapaotai in Aoyu Street Township in the fourth district and Laohushan in Fenghuang Town in the first district, most of them are Yizhong (charitable burial grounds). If mulberry trees are planted in all of them, it will affect the graves. It seems that we should find ways to maintain and determine the principle of protection. Resolution:　Do not plant in places where graves are densely distributed and mulberry trees cannot be planted.　When planting mulberry trees, the Provincial Silkworm Seed Manufacturing Institute should cooperate with the township head of Fenghuang Town in the first district and the township head of Aoyu Township in the fourth district.　In all official wasteland areas, if there are those who have already reported to the Jiangdu County Government and have a formal management license for the land, they should all be given way.　In the official wasteland area, if the two townships where the public cemetery system will be implemented in the future have no other land available for the construction of a public cemetery, after the two districts request the county government to forward the request to the provincial department for approval, the original silkworm seed manufacturing institute will withdraw a portion for the construction of a public cemetery.

Local News

The Shanghai Branch of the Sino-Soviet Cultural Association was Established Yesterday, Passing the Branch's Rules and Electing the President and Directors 96

The Shanghai Branch of the Sino-Soviet Cultural Association held its inaugural meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. The attendees included Soviet Consul-General in Shanghai, Bin尔维尼, as well as Chu Minyi, Zeng Shengdian, Yang Weiyu, Fu Donghua, Li Dachao, Ouyang Yuqian, Zhou Jianyun, Mei Lanfang, Gan Yansheng, Zai Yachen, Peng Hu, Yang Yinpu, Li Gongpu, Zhou Gucheng, Zhang Naiqi, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Shouqian, Li Zhaohuan, and the General Association Representative Zhang Ximan, City Government Representative Zhang Yuanruo, City Party Headquarters Representative Tong Xingbai, and Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, among over forty others. Li Zhaohuan was elected as the chairman.

Meeting Agenda:

All stood at attention.　Bowed three times to the national flags of China and the Soviet Union.　The Chairman respectfully read the Prime Minister's will.　The Chairman delivered the opening remarks.　Report on the preparation process and proposal of the charter.　Election of the branch president.　Election of directors.　Speech by the General Association President.　Speech by the Soviet Consul-General.　Speech by Mayor Wu.　Speech by the City Party Headquarters Representative.　Speech by the Education Bureau Director.　Ceremony completed.　Photography.　Refreshments.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremonial procedures, Chairman Li Zhaohuan reported, "After the establishment of the General Association of the Sino-Soviet Cultural Association in the capital, due to the number of members in Shanghai exceeding sixty or seventy, Mr. Zhang Shouyong, Chu Minyi, Wang Xiaolai, and others actively prepared to establish a branch. After obtaining approval from the party and government agencies, it was decided at the last preparatory meeting to establish it today. Currently, the number of members has reached one hundred and two. The preparatory committee also elected Zhang Shouyong, Wang Xiaolai, and myself as the presidium. We are very grateful for the attendance and guidance of the party and government agencies and higher-level officials. According to the charter, a president and directors should be elected to preside over the association's affairs."

Passing of the Charter

The branch charter was then passed: "(1) This branch, in accordance with the resolution of the General Association's Third Directors' Meeting, shall have one president, eleven directors, and six alternate directors, forming a board of directors. It may also appoint two honorary presidents. The president, directors, and alternate directors shall be elected by the members of this branch for a term of one year, and may be re-elected. If the president of this branch is unable to exercise his powers due to any reason, the board of directors may elect one person to act on his behalf. (2) This branch shall have one secretary and one accountant to handle affairs, and shall temporarily establish four group leaders for cultural exchange, deliberation, and publicity, appointing members to concurrently serve in these roles. Other staff members may be employed depending on the complexity of the affairs. The secretary, accountant, and group leaders are honorary positions and shall not be paid salaries. (3) The secretary and accountant shall handle daily affairs under the president's orders. The group leaders shall handle the affairs of their respective groups under the president's orders and the secretary's guidance. (4) The secretary and accountant may attend meetings. The group leaders may attend meetings if their attendance is approved by the president due to their involvement in the matters. (5) Within the scope of the General Association's charter, this branch may organize various activities and report them to the General Association. However, important matters must be approved by the General Association in advance before they can be held. (6) This branch has the responsibility to jointly conduct association affairs with the General Association and other branches. (7) All resolutions of this branch's Directors' Meeting must be reported to the General Association for record. (8) Shanghai residents who support the aims of this association may become members of this association after being introduced by three members of this association, filling out two membership application forms, and being approved by the board of directors of this branch. The branch shall submit one copy of the membership application form to the General Association for record. (9) Members shall pay a membership fee of two yuan upon joining and an annual membership fee of two yuan. (10) This branch is financially independent. All membership fees payable from Shanghai shall be allocated to the branch by the General Association for subsidies. The remainder shall be raised by the branch itself. (11) This branch does not establish its own charter, but may participate in elections and submit opinions on amending the charter in the name of the branch at the General Association's annual members' meeting. (12) These rules shall come into effect after being passed by the members of this branch and shall be sent to the General Association for record."

Election of President

Li Zhaohuan was then elected as president. Pan Gongzhan, Jiao Jihua, Li Gongpu, Ouyang Zhiwu, Fang Huanru, Du Yuesheng, Lin Bosheng, Wang Xiaolai, Chu Minyi, Zhang Shouyong, Ou Yuanhuai, and others were elected as directors. Huang Renzhi, Chen Han, Zhou Jianyun, Lu Ganchen, Chen Heqin, Zai Yachen, and others were elected as alternate directors.

Representatives' Speeches

General Association Representative Zhang Ximan then delivered a speech, "I am very honored to represent the General Association of the Sino-Soviet Cultural Association and President Sun Ke to attend today's grand meeting and congratulate the Shanghai Branch on its establishment. We all know that the two countries are geographically contiguous for over 20,000 li. This single natural geographical condition is sufficient to prove the close relationship between the two major countries in terms of politics and economics. Moreover, China and the Soviet Union are countries that uphold world peace and justice and are contributing their full efforts to economic construction and the improvement of cultural life. If China and the Soviet Union can work together in communicating Eastern and Western cultures, we can make tremendous progress on the path to increasing the happiness of humanity in the world. This major historical mission is falling on the shoulders of the cultural circles of the Republic of China and the Soviet Union. The members of this association will surely harvest the results of this great historical mission with their own heroic achievements."

Soviet Consul's Speech

Soviet Consul Bin尔维尼 then delivered a speech, "Gentlemen, Ambassador Bao is busy in Beijing and cannot come here to attend your association's grand ceremony. Therefore, I am here to offer my congratulations. The cultural circles of China and the Soviet Union, in order to express the importance of national friendship, civilization, and culture, recently established the General Association of the Sino-Soviet Cultural Association in Beijing, enthusiastically demonstrating its mission. Today's establishment of the Shanghai Branch is a sign of its efforts towards a great goal, which will gather the research of many people in order to communicate the cultures of the two countries. I hereby congratulate your association's progress after its establishment and wish you good results and plans."

Party and Government Addresses

City Government Representative Zhang Yuanruo then delivered a speech, "Mayor Wu has always warmly supported cultural undertakings. Today, he is unable to attend due to other commitments. Culture has a close relationship with the nation and the individual, directly and indirectly. Its significance, in essence, is the survival, development, and improvement of the environment of the nation, and it has a major relationship with the development of the country and the nation. Culture is the expression of the nation's soul and the element that maintains life. Therefore, I hope that after the establishment of your association, you will contribute more to society and the country." Tong Xingbai then gave a speech, the main idea of which was that the significance of the establishment was to seek friendship between the countries and communication of culture, and that they should take on this great responsibility in the future in order to benefit both China and the Soviet Union. Finally, Pan Gongzhan gave a speech, briefly stating, "China and the Soviet Union are both ancient civilizations with deep cultural ties. I sincerely hope that through the efforts of your association, the cultures of the two countries will achieve further communication and development."

Silk Improvement Association: Purchasing Silkworm Eggs and Mulberry Seedlings for Distribution to Silkworm Farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces; Weak Overseas Silk Market and Few Factories Operating in Shanghai 97

The Dagong News Agency reports: The National Economic Council's Silk Improvement Association, in view of the nationwide silk factories closing down one after another last year due to a lack of raw materials, and in order to seek remedies, has already, together with the Construction Departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces, purchased a large quantity of silkworm eggs from abroad and also acquired 500,000 mulberry seedlings, which are being distributed to silkworm farmers in various places for cultivation. The number of silk factories operating in Shanghai is still very small. Details are noted below:

Expanding Mulberry Fields: The Silk Improvement Association, recognizing the active export of domestically produced raw silk last year, but because silk factories lacked raw materials, resulting in insufficient reeling and subsequent forced shutdowns, and in order to seek remedies, this year specially dispatched personnel to Italy and Japan to purchase over one million sheets of silkworm eggs, which were handed over to the Construction Departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces for distribution to silkworm farmers in various places. Furthermore, due to the sharp increase in silkworm eggs, the existing mulberry gardens will inevitably be insufficient for allocation, so over 500,000 mulberry seedlings were purchased from the Nanjing and Zhejiang Sericulture Model Farms (at a cost of 1.3 cents per seedling) and distributed to the Construction Departments of the two provinces, for transfer to the silkworm farmer guidance centers, for silkworm farmers to purchase and plant. As for mulberry fields, over 2,000 acres have been opened up in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang regions, so it is anticipated that when the spring silkworms emerge this year, there will be no further shortage of raw materials.

Sluggish Silk Market: In the overseas silk market, Shanghai white filature silk could be sold for over 900 yuan per picul in November of last year, but by the end of December, it had begun to decline, falling to around 800 yuan. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of the year, it has become even more sluggish. Currently, the market price in Europe and America for Shanghai white filature silk is only around 720 yuan per picul. Since the factories in this city closed for the year-end accounting, they have remained closed due to a lack of raw materials and the weak silk prices, so very few have resumed operation. Currently, it is estimated that only the following have resumed operation: Jiyu (積餘) in the Xin Zha district, 240 spinning machines on Gonghe Road; Yihe (怡和) on Chengdu Road, 248 machines; Baotai (寶泰) in the South Shanghai area, 200 machines; and the Fulun (福綸) double-cocoon silk factory in the Hongkou area. All other factories have no news of resuming operation. It is generally expected that a decision will be made after the spring silkworms emerge in June.

Dutch East Indies: Preferential Treatment for the Import of Chinese Goods, Issuance of Special Import Permits 98

The Xinsheng News Agency reports: According to news from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, since the Dutch East Indies government implemented the regulations restricting the import of goods, import merchants for products from various countries on the restricted list must submit the amount of imports for the five years (from 1929 to 1933) to the Economic Department of the Dutch East Indies government for review and approval. Now, special preferential treatment is given to the import of Chinese products, and an additional special import permit has been issued (this permit is only for Chinese products), and the regulations are as follows: All Chinese goods imported with a permit must have a cargo list certified by the exporting government office and the Dutch consul residing in China for identification.
