Request to Reduce Coal Tax Rates: Ministry of Finance Approves Deferral for Discussion, Considering That There is Currently No Need for This; Will Reconsider When Tax Reduction Becomes Necessary in the Future 100

The National Mining Association, citing the increasingly declining business of the industry and the inability to maintain operations, submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance last month, requesting that the mineral tax rate for coal be gradually reduced to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and benefit the mining industry. The association received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, document number 8556, which stated: The presentation dated January 88, 25th year, regarding the continued request to gradually reduce the mineral tax rate for coal, and requesting prompt approval and implementation, has been received. The Ministry has been collecting coal mineral taxes at a rate of 5%, which has not exceeded the scope stipulated by the Mining Law. Judging from the current situation of various coal mines paying taxes, the highest tax is no more than 45 cents per ton, and the lowest is only 12 cents. Compared with the simultaneous collection of mining taxes and mineral taxes by the former Beijing Ministry of Finance, the burden has actually been greatly reduced. The Ministry has repeatedly improved the mineral tax, such as allowing refunds under the mineral tax for all mines that have been charged transit taxes by the customs since the 22nd year. In July of the 23rd year, the Ministry also allowed the refund of the originally collected mineral tax based on the export tax receipts for coal sold overseas. Recently, the Ministry has also directly exempted the customs transit tax on goods that have already paid the mineral tax, in order to alleviate the difficulties of cumbersome tax payment and refund procedures and the pain of capital stagnation. All these measures are intended to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and support the real economy. Now that the burden on mining businesses has gradually been reduced, and the import taxes on foreign coal have been repeatedly increased, there is already sufficient protection for the domestic coal mining industry. The association's request to gradually reduce the mineral tax rate for coal is deemed by the Ministry to be unnecessary in the current situation. If the situation changes in the future and a tax reduction becomes necessary, it will be reviewed and processed accordingly. Please be informed.

Situation in Tokyo from Sino-Japanese Wireless Telephone 103

Dentsu News Agency, Director Tian Talks with Shanghai Branch Dentsu News Agency (1st) from this city's report, since the morning of the 26th when the attack on various government offices occurred in Japan's capital, communication between this city and Japan was cut off for a time, resulting in various rumors and the suffering of not knowing the truth of the incident. Now the incident has been completely resolved as of yesterday, and communication facilities have also been restored. Therefore, Ueda Sakuzo, Managing Director of Dentsu News Agency, used the Sino-Japanese money-free telephone this morning to report the situation in Tokyo to the Shanghai branch. The questions and answers between Director Ueda and the Shanghai branch are as follows: (Ueda) After the incident, there have been various unstable rumors, I fear that you feel uneasy, but the security in Tokyo is better than usual, the order is very good, so there is no unease. However, for a time, because telegrams and telephones were not available, news etc. could not pass through as usual, and it is a pity that the responsibilities of the news agency could not be fully utilized. Yesterday from 5:00 a.m. to 2:00 p.m., traffic between Tokyo and the outside was completely cut off, so this company took contact with the Yokohama branch and sent news from Yokohama to various parts of the country and overseas. (Branch) What are the deaths and injuries of this decision incident? (Ueda) Only important people such as Takahashi, Saito, Watanabe, etc., and only 5 police officers died in the line of duty, but all of them were guarding the Prime Minister's official residence and other government offices. Not a single civilian or police officer in the city was killed or injured. (Branch) Were there any deaths or injuries when suppressing the rebellious soldiers? (Ueda) Of course, not a single shot was fired, and everything was completely stabilized, so there were no deaths or injuries. Rather than saying it was due to force, mother Ning's advice was effective. (Branch) How do you observe the organization of the successor cabinet? (Ueda) Who organizes the successor cabinet, there is nothing to say in the current state, and the successor to the deceased Saito Naifu is the first question, and Admiral Kawai Osamu, etc., from the Privy Council, are calling for a higher voice, but the general atmosphere is that those who come are not suitable to be biased towards one party and one faction, and rely solely on the power of one side, so it should be a unified and powerful cabinet for the country, that is, an ideal cabinet that can boast both internally and externally. The appearance of such a cabinet is what the general public hopes for, and the military will not disagree. As for the political parties, the Minsei Party goes without saying, and the Seiyukai has also taken a supportive attitude, so if they wish to enter the cabinet, they can recommend party members.

Customs Announces Foreign Trade for January: National Import of Foreign Goods Declines, While Export of Domestic Goods is Active, Especially Tung Oil Exports 105

Shen Shi News Agency reports: In January of this year, the national foreign trade surplus was over 9 million, as reported in previous newspapers. The reason for the surplus was the decline in imports of foreign goods. Imports of rice, wheat, metals, and minerals have decreased significantly. At the same time, exports of domestic goods were more active, especially tung oil exports. We have inquired with the Customs for details, as follows:

Major Foreign Goods Are Weakening

According to the Customs announcement, in January of this year, the national foreign trade saw a sharper decline in imports of foreign goods than before. The value of major imports is weakening. Cotton: 25,383,295 yuan, compared to 54,692,56 yuan in the same period last year. Wool and its products: 14,304,422 yuan, compared to 16,560,11 yuan in the same period last year. Metals and minerals: 63,527,26 yuan, compared to 93,439,64 yuan in the same period last year. Machinery and tools: 48,610,35 yuan, compared to 57,129,46 yuan in the same period last year. Miscellaneous metal products: 27,445,95 yuan, compared to 35,663,17 yuan in the same period last year. Foreign rice: 976,136 yuan, compared to 91,663,00 yuan in the same period last year. Wheat: 513,278 yuan, compared to 49,709,99 yuan in the same period last year. Fish and seafood products: 17,517,05 yuan, compared to 22,663,80 yuan in the same period last year. Paint and diesel: 13,376,05 yuan, compared to 19,705,32 yuan in the same period last year. Paper: 36,549,99 yuan, compared to 53,455,84 yuan in the same period last year. Wood: 713,387 yuan, compared to 33,194,40 yuan in the same period last year. In addition, only the imports of kerosene, chemicals, dyes, etc., have increased slightly compared to last year. The total value of imports in January was 60,950,296 yuan.

Tung Oil Exports Are the Most Active

The exports of domestic goods in January were more active. The value of major exports is recorded as follows: Pig bristles: 1,268,891 yuan. Eggs and egg products: 1,540,265 yuan. Raw and processed hides and leather goods: 4,917,895 yuan. Soybeans: 589,666 yuan. Bran: 396,282 yuan. Rice grains: 299,237 yuan. Cottonseed oil: 705,478 yuan. Tung oil: 8,813,465 yuan. Sesame: 3,901,561 yuan. Tea: 2,032,161 yuan. Tobacco leaves: 1,137,425 yuan. Cotton: 4,316,792 yuan. Silk: 4,829,502 yuan. Cotton yarn: 1,928,807 yuan. Silk fabrics: 1,926,692 yuan. Antimony: 465,268 yuan. Most of the exported domestic goods have increased compared to before, and tung oil exports are particularly active. The total value of exports in January was 70,669,258 yuan.

The Xin Xin News Agency reports: Former Mayor of Nanjing Wei Daoming recently entered Beijing from Shanghai to continue seeking instructions from President Chiang. Hu Decides to Come North

The reporter asked Wei about the rumors about Hu Hanmin's coming north, which have been circulating in recent days, causing much speculation and confusion. According to Wei, Mr. Hu is still staying in Guangdong Province. The reason why he has not come north is purely due to the climate and there are no other special reasons. As soon as the weather here is warmer, Mr. Hu will be able to prepare to depart and come north. As for the rumors that Mr. Hu must wait to meet Mr. Wang Liangchou before coming north together, it is unfounded. The opinions of Beijing and Guangdong are very harmonious, and there is no need for so-called mediation.

Metered Telephone Charges in the Concession: After the Implementation of the New Regulations 109

The Dagong News Agency reports: The new regulations for metered telephone charges in the Special District of this city came into effect as scheduled yesterday. The telephone company is currently considering the issue of installing meter counters. The Special District Telephone Issue Committee, in order to resolutely resist, specially announced to users throughout the city yesterday to implement the claim and replied to the city's federated branch that it would not disband and would continue to proceed. Details are explored as follows:

The New Telephone Regulations Come into Effect as Scheduled

The period for the Shanghai Telephone Company's new metered charging regulations in the Special District has ended yesterday. The telephone company's procedures for implementing the new regulations were prepared long ago. In addition to repeatedly notifying users, from 1:00 am yesterday, the company's Jiangxi Road Central Station in the Public Concession area, and the seven branch stations in the West District's Medhurst Road, the East District's Hongqiao Road and Ward Road, the Central District's Fujian Road, the North District's North Jiangxi Road, and the South District's Ba Liqiao Road and Bi Xun Road in the French Concession area, installed a total meter of 48,617 active user machines in the administered districts and activated them at the same time. Except for business users who communicate with the company, the new regulations apply to both business and residential phones.

Company Authorities Consider Installing Meters

Although the Municipal Council and the Shanghai Telephone Company authorities have stated that they cannot change the new regulations in the face of opposition from all parties, according to reporters' inquiries with the company, the Municipal Council Board of Directors has indicated that it may accept the suggestions from all parties to install automatic meter counters next to the phone of each user. They recently transferred a discussion to the highest authority of the telephone company to solicit opinions on technical aspects of this issue. The company has a large number of users and would be very burdened to separately install such sub-meters, but in order not to run counter to the users' wishes, they will consider it so that it can be formally submitted to the Municipal Council for review in the future.

Telephone Committee Notifies Users

The Special District Telephone Issue Committee, composed of various groups in this city, specially issued an emergency announcement to all users in the Special District yesterday in order to implement its claim and resolutely resist the ineffectiveness of negotiations against metered billing: We are informing you that the Shanghai Telephone Company's new regulations have been implemented since the 1st, and all our users have been burdened with additional charges since that day. Although this committee has repeatedly negotiated with the Municipal Council and the Shanghai Telephone Company, it is useless as they take advantage of the expansion of external forces and hold power, ignoring public opinion. Furthermore, the Chinese Ratepayers Association had repeatedly stated and requested the Chinese directors to come forward to negotiate, requesting to increase the basic count, although it failed to meet the wishes of the citizens, it was somewhat comforting to us. However, the recent claim has suddenly changed, and they have indicated that they may accept the company's new charging regulations. Yesterday's newspaper reported that the association solemnly stated that "there has never been any intention to recognize or accept it" and advocated "not using" it as a manifestation of the facts. This committee has repeatedly decided to propose discussions at the meeting, and there is a question about whether the users throughout the city have this firm solidarity power. Therefore, we are now sending letters to various sectors of society. If you can allow the phone to be removed, it would be a thorough view. If you must use the phone in practice, please record it at any time during use and fill in the date and type separately to make a statistics. At the end of this month, submit the form for calculating the settlement to the meeting as a basis. This committee will uphold the spirit of the past and do its utmost to seek the final victory for all users. As for all the proceedings, we still hope that all sectors of society will not hesitate to give advice. We are sincerely looking forward to it. We salute you with our best wishes.

Responding to the City Federation Expresses Striving

The Telephone Issue Committee sent a letter to the citizens' branches of each district in this city yesterday: We are responding to your letter. We have learned everything. Regarding the preparation of this committee to dissolve, according to the organizational law, it must be decided by a joint meeting of various groups. Before dissolution, we will naturally adhere to our consistent aim and continue to fight. We are grateful for all the suggestions from your association, which will be submitted to the scheduled meeting on the 10th of this month for discussion in order to obtain a thorough solution.

Smuggled Foreign Silk Discovered in Freight Car of the Joint Ping-Hu Army; Estimated Value of Ten Large Packages is Ten Thousand Gold 112

Yesterday (1st) morning, a freight car of the joint Ping-Hu (Peiping-Shanghai) army arrived carrying a large quantity of smuggled foreign silk, totaling ten large packages, each containing thirty small packages, with an estimated value of ten thousand gold. Chen Guoliang, the station's chief stationmaster, ordered workers to unload the goods into the express delivery room, intending to wait for the consignee to arrive and then send them to customs for processing together. After a while, three foreigners arrived with several hired cargo trucks and delivery orders, insisting on claiming the goods. Stationmaster Chen refused to release the goods due to the case involving the smuggling of a large quantity of taxable silk, and telegraphed the customs to send personnel to the station. After much negotiation, the foreign businessmen agreed to accompany the customs officials and transport the smuggled artificial silk together to the customs for verification.

Peddler Suddenly Dies While Being Pursued by Western Police; Western Police Admit to Hitting Him Twice; Cause of Death Unknown, Requires Autopsy 121

As reported in previous newspapers, at around 8:00 AM on the 28th of last month, a peddler of unknown name, aged over thirty, was selling stationery in front of the Chengzong Middle School on Tangshan Road when a Western police officer No. 132 from the Huishan Police Station arrived in a police car, intending to arrest the peddler. The peddler, fearing arrest, fled to the kitchen of the Yuda Store behind the Yangzheng Middle Lane (No. 413 Tangshan Road). The Western police officer also chased after him. Shortly after, the peddler suddenly collapsed in the house, unconscious. He was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died. The body was taken to the morgue on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Song Genshan, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by two medical examiners, Wei and Zhang, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. He then took the case. The Western police chief, Philip, reported that at 8:00 AM yesterday morning, the deceased and several peddlers were gambling in front of a school on Tangshan Road, so the police station sent Western police officer No. 132 to arrest them. The deceased, seeing the police arrive, was extremely frightened and fled to the back door of No. 413. Due to the sudden stimulation of running forty-four feet, he collapsed. He requested that the body be autopsied. Wang Zian, 21 years old, from Nanjing, who works at the Yuda Store at No. 413 Tangshan Road, testified that when the Western police officer chased after the deceased, he fled to the back door of his store. He was behind the counter, so he did not see the Western police officer hit him. A maid living on the upper floor witnessed everything. Shen Wu, 32 years old, from Huzhou, who works as a maid on the upper floor of the store, testified that yesterday morning, she was near the handrail and saw a peddler running to the back of her house with a basket. The Western police officer chased after him and asked whose basket he was carrying. He begged and said it was his. The Western police officer hit his face twice with his hand. When the police officer was about to leave, the deceased suddenly collapsed. Seeing this, she shouted, and the police officer came back and pressed a wet towel on his face several times, but he did not wake up. The police officer then sent him to the hospital in his car. Western police officer No. 132, named Bass, a British national, 28 years old, admitted to lightly patting the deceased's jaw twice. Mr. Song then ruled that the cause of death of the deceased, whose name is unknown, was unclear and should be autopsied by the court's medical examiner for further verification. Since the family of the deceased has not arrived, the body will be handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial after the autopsy.

State-Run China Merchants Bureau Implements Reform Measures; Layoffs of Redundant Staff Have Been Implemented; Elimination of Long-Standing Malpractices Awaits Progress 122

According to the Shenshi News Agency, after the internal reorganization of the state-run China Merchants Bureau and the abolition of the Supervisory Committee, Cai Zengji, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau, Tan Boying, General Manager of the Xingye Trust Company, and Lao Mian, sent by the Ministry of Communications, were appointed as General Manager and Deputy Managers to vigorously rectify all the Bureau's operations. The reform steps of the Bureau are as follows:

Laying off Redundant Staff to Save Expenses

The past situation of the state-run China Merchants Bureau was due to excessive staff and huge expenses. Therefore, although revenue had slightly increased, it was still insufficient to cover the wasteful expenditures. Therefore, laying off redundant staff was an urgent task. After taking office, Mr. Cai and others followed the newly promulgated organizational regulations of the Ministry of Communications to conduct recruitment examinations in order to strictly lay off staff to meet actual needs. Although all the Bureau's staff initially opposed it, they eventually complied with the order to take the examination. Now the oral and written examinations have been completed, and the staff to be laid off or retained have been submitted to the Ministry for approval and announcement.

The Comprador System Will Be Abolished

In addition, the Bureau's comprador system has been the biggest obstacle to the development of its business. For example, the practice of contracting passenger tickets and soliciting as many passengers as possible often resulted in temporary structures being erected outside the designated berths, causing overcrowding. This not only posed a danger to travelers but also harmed the Bureau's revenue and passengers' interests. The malpractice was extremely serious and should be thoroughly abolished. All business will be directly managed by the Bureau. It is currently being planned.

Abolish Contracting and Strictly Prohibit Theft and Leakage

In addition, the cargo warehouse contracting system is also the easiest to steal and leak. Because the cargo warehouse business of the Bureau has always been contracted by the warehouse manager, the Bureau cannot directly manage it. There are often cases of falsely demanding money from merchants. And for the labor force, the warehouse manager contracts it to the foreman, and the foreman then hires the porters, resulting in layers of exploitation, so that the laborers cannot get a reasonable wage and become increasingly poor. Theft and leakage occur as a result. Therefore, this contracting system is also being planned for cancellation.

Eliminate Malpractices of Stewards and Sailors

The stewards and sailors on all ships of the Bureau have always been hired by compradors. They only need to have cash deposits as a guarantee to be qualified, resulting in uneven quality and limited knowledge. There are often cases of insulting passengers, stealing passenger goods, privately selling berths, demanding exorbitant wine fees, smuggling drugs, trafficking in people, and engaging in corruption and fraud. This has a great impact on the company's business and national discipline. At the time of vigorously implementing the New Life Movement, this malpractice should also be immediately corrected. The Bureau will strictly examine the stewards and sailors on all ships in the future and thoroughly reform them.

The City's Severe Cold Has Not Abated; Wind Direction Has Changed, Warming Up in the Next Few Days; Prices of Vegetables and Other Items Have Doubled 123

The severe cold in the city since yesterday morning has not abated. The northwest wind continued to blow yesterday, causing the water pipes to freeze completely. The ditches along the roads in shaded areas were frozen until noon. Most of the inland rivers were also frozen, causing a sharp decrease in the number of vegetable boats coming to Shanghai from Suzhou River. The market prices of vegetables in various small vegetable markets suddenly increased more than twice. Chinese cabbage costs more than 500 copper coins per catty. The temperature is still around 24 degrees. According to astronomical sources, the high pressure has now left the country. The wind may turn to the southeast in the afternoon, and it may warm up in the next few days.

Sang Quansan Sentenced to Imprisonment for False Accusation of Public Officials; The Plaintiff's Incidental Civil Lawsuit Rejected 124

Sang Quansan, a Ningbo native who lives at No. 5, Lane 217, Tongfu Road, West Shanghai, and runs a military uniform business, borrowed eight pieces of jewelry from his fellow villager Xu Zhiliang in June of last year to raise money in an emergency. He did not return them for a long time. Xu then asked Wang Xiaoliang, a comprador from the Hongsheng Foreign Firm, to negotiate with Sang and lend him money to retrieve the jewelry. However, Sang suddenly had the idea of swallowing the jewelry, claiming that the jewelry originally belonged to him and was worth more than 20,000 gold. He said that Wang bought the jewelry from him and agreed on a price, but Wang only gave him more than 4,300 yuan when he took the jewelry, intending to default on the remaining payment. Wang and Xu said that Sang coveted the jewelry and fabricated nonsense. At that time, the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, considering the friendship between villagers, convened Sang, Wang, Xu, and others to mediate. Sang claimed that the jewelry was originally mortgaged to him by Xu, but he could not produce evidence of the mortgage. Xu then stated that he had indeed asked Sang to mortgage the jewelry to a certain bank on his behalf, but he had redeemed it on time. He was grateful to Sang for his economic assistance, so he generously lent him the jewelry. He did not expect Sang to repay kindness with ingratitude and try to embezzle it. The mediators, having understood the situation, did not side with Sang, and the mediation failed. Sang still did not give up and filed a criminal self-lawsuit against Wang Xiaoliang and Xu Zhiliang in the First Special District Court, accusing Wang and Xu of conspiring to defraud him of the jewelry and requesting that they be punished for fraud. He also filed an incidental civil lawsuit, requesting that the two defendants be ordered to repay the owed amount of 16,667 yuan or return the original jewelry. After being accused, Wang and Xu also hired lawyers to state the course of the dispute, claiming that Sang was actually trying to embezzle the jewelry, fabricating a lawsuit, and requesting that it be rejected. They also requested that he be severely punished according to the law for the crime of false accusation, to warn against cunning and treacherous behavior. Judge Ye Shengchao of the First Special Court repeatedly held hearings and investigated the evidence in detail for more than a month. Recently, it was finally concluded. The verdict was announced in court the day before yesterday afternoon. The main points were that Sang Quansan intended to cause others to be subject to criminal punishment, falsely accused the competent public officials, and was sentenced to two months of imprisonment. Wang Xiaoliang and Xu Zhiliang were both innocent. The plaintiff's incidental civil lawsuit was rejected.

The City's Movement to Free Female Servants Began Yesterday; Registering Female Servants Means Restoring Freedom; Those Who Resist Liberation Will Be Dealt With According to Law 125

The city's movement to free female servants began yesterday. The Municipal Public Security Bureau has begun registering those who keep female servants. The investigation period is four months. During the investigation period, those who keep female servants should apply to the Bureau for registration. Female servants may also apply for registration themselves or entrust others to do so on their behalf. Female servants who have been registered will be unconditionally liberated and regain their freedom. If they are minors and have no home to return to, or if they return home but their families cannot afford to support them, they may be sent to the city's relief home or other charitable organizations for placement. Female servants who are over sixteen years old and have no home to return to may be arranged for marriage with their consent. Those who keep female servants beyond the prescribed investigation period and do not apply for registration may be fined up to ten yuan and ordered to complete the registration. Moreover, those who keep female servants who have been registered and resist liberation will be sent to the judicial organs for handling according to law. Therefore, all households in the city that keep female servants should comply with the deadline and apply to the respective branch offices for registration. The registration of female servants began yesterday, and the registration period is four months, ending at the end of June.

Ministry of Communications Orders the Directorate General of Posts to Strictly Investigate Smuggling of Drugs; Newspapers and Magazines Are Being Noticed 126

According to the Shenshi News Agency, the Ministry of Communications approved the National Anti-Smoking Supervisory Office's letter No. 34, which stated that Mr. Hu Shize, the representative of our country at the 20th session of the League of Nations Opium Advisory Committee, reported that it has been heard that the United States recently discovered cases of smuggling, many of which involved narcotics and opium being inserted into newspapers and magazines and sent by Chinese post offices. The letter requested that all post offices across the country be thoroughly investigated and reported. After approving the letter, the Ministry of Communications forwarded it to the Directorate General of Posts, ordering all post offices across the country to comply and strictly investigate. The Shanghai Postal Administration has received the order from the Directorate General and has been very strict in inspecting parcels containing newspapers and magazines in recent days.

Electrical Manufacturing Industry Discusses the Copper Shortage Problem; Hosts Banquet Yesterday for Mr. Wang Jiliang, a Mining Engineer Who Studied in the United States; Lectures on the Overview of the Daye and Yangxin Copper Mines 127

The Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association believes that the need for copper in electrical manufacturing plants is extremely large, but there is no clear record of copper production in our country in the world mineral production records. Since the price increase last year, the price of copper has gradually soared. Old copper scraps have been exhausted, and Shanghai copper skin factories are almost at a standstill. However, the demand is increasing, forming a copper shortage. The Association, thinking from the root cause, paid attention to the study of copper mines. Yesterday, Mr. Hu Xiyuan, Chairman of the Association, and Lin Chaote, Director-General, hosted a banquet at the Shipping Club for Mr. Wang Jiliang, a mining engineer who studied in the United States, and invited him to lecture on the overview of the Daye and Yangxin copper mines in Hubei Province. According to Mr. Wang, the mining area is 30 li wide, and the transportation is very convenient. If large-scale mining is carried out, 50 tons of copper can be produced every day. A part of our country's copper needs can be self-sufficient. According to the survey conducted by the Association, Shanghai alone needs more than 4,000 dan of copper skin per month for flashlight factories, and 500,000 pounds of copper sheets and copper wires per year for electric fans and motors. In addition, the amount needed for national defense and light and heavy industries is more than ten or a hundred times this amount.

Zhenjiang Power Plant Machinery Damaged, Huasheng Factory Sends Technicians to Repair

Zhenjiang is the capital of Jiangsu Province, with a dense population of households. The electricity business is developing rapidly. On the 17th of last month, the core of the large generator of the Dazhao Electric Company in that area suddenly broke down. Unable to find a solution locally, they urgently telegraphed the Huasheng Electric Manufacturing Factory in Shanghai, requesting that personnel be sent quickly to repair it. Sister and Brother in Litigation

Wu, the wife of Yang Weilan, had some savings. Her husband had passed away many years ago. Yang Wu's biological mother, Wu Chen, suddenly fell ill last year on the first month of the lunar year and passed away on the 23rd of the twelfth month. Her son, Chang Liushun, never came to visit. After Yang Wu notified Liushun, he ignored it. As a result, Yang Wu held the funeral, spending more than a thousand yuan on medical and funeral expenses. She repeatedly sought reimbursement from Liushun without success. Yang Wu then retained lawyer Shen Zongyong to file a lawsuit with the First Special Court, seeking to recover the funds. The court approved the request. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Yuhai presided over the hearing in the Fourth Tribunal. First, the plaintiff recounted the events. The defendant argued that Wu Chen was not his biological mother, but that his biological mother was surnamed Li. However, after repeated questioning by Judge Zhang, he admitted that Wu Chen was indeed his biological mother and had passed away in November of last year, but claimed that he had not been notified by his sister and therefore did not know about it. Judge Zhang, finding that Wu Liushun lacked human ethics and reason, advised him to go outside and negotiate a settlement to end the lawsuit. Unexpectedly, Wu Liushun was very stubborn. Judge Zhang then ordered everyone to withdraw and await instructions. After the court adjourned, Wu Liushun guarded the door of the decision chamber, claiming that he wanted to get his sister and be satisfied. Judge Zhang, fearing a fight, ordered Wu Shunliu to be separated from Yang Wu and sent away.

Yesterday Onwards: Prohibition of Live Plucking of Pig Bristles; Joint Announcement by the Three Bureaus of Public Safety, Social Affairs, and Public Health; Pig Merchants Send Representatives to Board Ships and Cut Bristles, Maintaining Good Order 130

The Huadong News Agency reports that the issue of prohibiting the live plucking of pig bristles has been a long-standing dispute. Previously, the Social Affairs Bureau, together with the Public Health and Public Safety Bureaus, convened relevant pig industry groups to discuss prohibition measures. These measures were implemented starting yesterday, and a public notice was posted yesterday morning as follows: "Live plucking of pig bristles is a cruel act and detrimental to meat hygiene, as has been repeatedly announced. However, it has been found that some individuals still privately engage in live plucking, deliberately violating the law. In addition to investigating and punishing such acts at any time, to eradicate this bad habit and eliminate the cruel act of live plucking for profit, this Bureau, in consultation with the other Bureaus, has decided that from March 1, 1936, all pigs transported to Shanghai must have their bristles cut off before being allowed to enter. Any live plucking of pig bristles will be considered animal cruelty and will be subject to a fine of five cents to five yuan, as stipulated in Article 7 of the Shanghai Slaughter Inspection Regulations. This decision has been reported to the Municipal Government for record, and all county governments in the areas where the pigs originate have been requested to instruct pig merchants to comply. All pig industry groups in Shanghai have also been instructed to comply. This joint announcement is hereby issued to urge everyone to abide by it and refrain from attempting to violate it, lest they be punished." Signed: Cai Jinjun, Director of the Public Safety Bureau; Wu Xingya, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau; Li Tingan, Director of the Public Health Bureau. In compliance with the order, various pig industry groups implemented the measures starting yesterday. The Pig Merchants Association specially dispatched 20 people to the pig ships at Wusongkou to assist in cutting off the uncut bristles. Personnel from the Public Health Bureau's office were also dispatched to supervise all arriving ships. All pig industry workers expressed their compliance with the above measures, so the order was well maintained. All the pig bristles were given to the boatmen of the ships, which was supported by all parties.

Rice Shop Owner Jiang Rongfu: Concubine Chen Demands Treatment as "Two Heads of the Family" with a Monthly Allowance of Sixty Yuan; Payments Suddenly Stopped, Leading to Lawsuit 131

Jiang Rongfu, a native of Jiading, is 59 years old and owns the Changhe Rice Shop on Niuzhuang Road. His concubine, Madam Chen, a Ningbo native (also 99 years old), residing at No. 2 Changqing Lane, Guoqing Road, has engaged lawyer Xu Wufang to file a lawsuit in the Civil Division of the First Special District Court, seeking alimony. The main points of her lawsuit are as follows: Madam Chen married the defendant at the age of 21 and held a wedding ceremony at the Qu family's Lao Yongxing Garden. However, after the marriage, she discovered that the defendant already had a wife. Since it was a fait accompli, there was nothing she could do. Therefore, the defendant treated her as "two heads of the family." Madam Chen bore two sons and two daughters. The son, named Chen Xia, is now 28 years old. One daughter is deceased, and the third daughter, named Mao Yuan, is now 19 years old. In 1922, because the defendant failed to fulfill his alimony obligations, Cang Zhisheng, the manager of the Xiechangde Rice Shop, mediated and stipulated that Madam Chen would receive a monthly living allowance of 60 yuan and five dou of rice. However, when the deceased daughter died, the defendant ignored all funeral expenses, which Madam Chen had to borrow from others. Recently, the defendant suddenly reduced the agreed monthly living allowance to 40 yuan. Since November of last year, he has not paid even the 40 yuan. Madam Chen sent her daughter Mao Yuan to demand payment, but to no avail. Therefore, she has no choice but to file a lawsuit, requesting the court to order the defendant to pay a monthly living allowance of 120 yuan, as well as 2,400 yuan in loans, and to bear the litigation costs. The case was heard in the 12th Civil Division of the First Special District Court by Judge Cao Jun the other day, and the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

Drug Trafficking: Zheng Tongcheng and Others Sentenced to Six Years Imprisonment; 25 Taels of Morphine Confiscated 132

Zheng Tongcheng from Fujian and Mao Ying (also known as Zhi Rui) from Wuxi conspired to secretly sell the drug morphine for profit. This was discovered by Sun Aizhong and Ji Peijin, Chinese detectives of the Huishan Police Station, who used an informant posing as a customer to arrange a drug exchange at 11 PM on the 16th of this month in Room 224 of the Andong Hotel, No. 131 Hubei Road. The suspects were arrested on the spot, along with 25 taels of morphine, worth over 500 yuan, and suspected accomplices Gu Linhai and Madam Liu Gu, both from Tongzhou. They confessed that the ringleader was Yu Zhiliang, who lived in Da'an Lane, Songshan Road, in the French Concession and was at large. They were ordered to await sentencing. The other day, Judge Jiang Shuzi presided over the Third Criminal Division and sentenced Zheng Tongcheng and Mao Ying to six years imprisonment each. Gu Linhai and Madam Liu Gu were released. The morphine was confiscated.

Ding Sun Dies from Coal Gas Poisoning; Gong Fengxian's Condition is Also Critical 134

Zhang Ziying from Changzhou used to work as a sample maker at the Customs. He recently moved to No. 22, Lane 159, Haige Road, in the French Concession. The other night, because he had just built a new stove, he used coal briquettes to dry it. At 11 PM, Ding Sunmin, a 32-year-old maid from Changzhou, and Gong Fengxian, Zhang's 11-year-old niece, went to sleep in the loft of the stove room. Yesterday morning at 6:30 AM, the rickshaw puller Zhang Yiqi got up and called out to the maid Sunmin to prepare breakfast. However, she did not respond despite repeated calls. Zhang suspected something was wrong and went upstairs to check. He saw that both Zhang and Gong Fengxian were foaming at the mouth and barely breathing. He realized they had been poisoned by coal gas. He immediately reported to his employer, who reported to the police. The police ordered the two to be taken to Guangci Hospital for treatment. However, Sunmin had been poisoned too deeply and died before she could be treated. Her body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall autopsy room to await examination. It is reported that Gong Fengxian's condition is very serious and she is also in danger.

This led to an argument, and Li Wansheng started hitting Wang and kicking him in the lower body. As a result, Wang's scrotum was injured, and he fell to the ground. Seeing the damage he had caused, Li fled the scene. The innkeeper reported the incident to the police, who sent detectives to take the injured man to the hospital for treatment. Detective Wang Dongwan arrested Li the other day and took him and the prostitute Wang Xiaomei to the police station. Improvement of Qimen Black Tea: Three Organizations Actively Working; All Equipment and Arrangements Completed; Quality of New Tea Expected to Improve This Year 139

The Shenshi News Agency reports that Anhui Province is famous for its tea production. Western Anhui is known for its green tea, while the black tea from Qimen and other places in southern Anhui is even more renowned internationally. The total annual export volume reaches 7-8 million dan, worth tens of millions of yuan, which is crucial to the rural economy. In the past, sales to the Soviet Union, Germany, and the United States often could not meet demand. However, in recent years, due to tea merchants adhering to old methods and failing to improve the tea-making and packaging, they have failed to meet the needs of foreign countries. In addition, competition from tea sales from Japan, India, and Java has impacted the international market, resulting in the loss of international market share year after year, and the tea industry has declined. In view of this, the Ministry of Industry, in cooperation with the National Sales Commission and the Anhui Provincial Government, has first established a Tea Improvement Center in Qimen, Anhui, to study and improve Qimen black tea using technical methods. The center is divided into technical and general affairs departments. The technical department is further divided into tea testing, cooperative promotion, packaging improvement, grading testing, and mechanical testing, to improve packaging methods and increase production quality. The machinery has been purchased from overseas. A large-scale tea farm and factory building have been built on Phoenix Mountain in the area, and local tea farmers have been recruited and given basic training. According to news from the tea industry in Shanghai, the equipment at the Qimen Improvement Center, which has been under preparation since last year, has now been arranged. The buildings and machinery are expected to be installed this month. It is expected that the new Qimen black tea will have a distinctive quality when it enters the market this year. On the one hand, it is also planned to cooperate with syndicates to promote cooperative societies, provide long-term loans for the tea industry, and assist tea farmers' economy, in order to increase production.

When the Dongjiadu Ferry Began Operations, More Than 300 Ferrymen Attempted to Riot; Police Suppression Prevented the Incident 140

The Dongjiadu Ferry in Nanshi was taken over by the Xingye Society yesterday (the 1st) and officially opened for business. On the first day of the ferry's operation, more than 300 former ferrymen gathered at both docks, one at Dongjiadu in Puxi and the other on the opposite bank in Pudong. They held printed materials (submissions) containing ten reasons from a certain Shanghai celebrity to the Municipal Government and distributed them to passersby, creating a turbulent atmosphere. Seeing this situation, the dock manager, fearing that an incident would occur, immediately closed the iron gate. After learning about the situation, the Water Police promptly dispatched several water police detectives to suppress the situation on both sides of the river. The Municipal Public Security Bureau also dispatched 70 officers from the Fourth Detachment to persuade the ferrymen to disperse. It was not until after 2 PM that the ferrymen were persuaded to disperse, and normal ferry operations resumed. Fortunately, no incident occurred.

Eight Thousand Football Fans Overjoyed: Donghua Wins the Scoto Cup Again; Portugal Suffers a Crushing Defeat of 3-1; Collacot Did Not Attend Yesterday Due to Injury 141

Donghua surprisingly defeated the strong Portugal team with an excellent performance yesterday to win the Scoto Cup and keep it for another year. The result, a 3-1 victory, overjoyed the eight thousand spectators at Yiyuan, who cheered wildly. Donghua's momentum was at its peak. Portuguese center Collacot did not attend due to injury, which weakened the Portuguese team considerably. The details of the fierce battle are as follows:

Two Goals Within Ten Minutes 142

Just after 2 PM, Yierbei Road was already packed with people. The east and west stands of Yiyuan were filled to capacity, totaling over eight thousand people. The atmosphere was intense, and everyone was discussing the strength of the two teams. When the two teams appeared, the Portuguese captain Collacot was indeed absent due to a foot injury, which relieved the concerned spectators. However, given Donghua's momentum yesterday, even if Collacot had been present, they would still have been able to secure victory. As can be seen from the details of the battle, after the kickoff, the Portuguese team took the lead, but it was immediately intercepted. Donghua's several advances were also blocked. After five or six minutes of stalemate, Donghua's army advanced from the center. Sun Jinshun broke through alone, dodging the defender and making a sweeping cross-kick, low, diagonal, and fast. Portuguese goalkeeper Max stared blankly, not knowing what to do. Donghua took the lead with a score of 1-0. At the center kickoff, Portuguese right winger Xiao Kaositan attacked along the side, but Li Ning met him with his abdomen, forcing a corner kick. At this time, the situation was dangerous. If Donghua had not taken precautions early, they would have been in trouble. The ball went to the right, and Donghua's five forwards swept in like a whirlwind. Zhou Guangzhong sent a cross-kick. Dai Linjing attacked together, and Sun Jinshun deflected the ball slightly, sending it into the net again. The score was 2-0, only eleven minutes after the start of the match.

Both Offense and Defense Presented Thrilling Moments; Donghua's Momentum Was at its Peak; Portuguese Goal Presented Many Dangerous Scenes 143

Donghua's momentum was at its peak, and after several maneuvers, the Portuguese goal presented many dangerous scenes. You Liang kicked a left shot at the side of the goal, but unfortunately, it leaked under the post. Lin Jing pulled back and shot fiercely, but it was saved by Marx. Losing two excellent chances caused the spectators to wring their hands in frustration. The Portuguese army launched many counterattacks, but to no avail. However, Donghua's fight also presented several dangerous scenes. Xiao Kaositan went all the way to the baseline and crossed the ball, but Shang Yi was unable to catch it. Fortunately, Li Ning headed the ball out of danger, and the ball returned to the center, becoming a chaotic battle again. Li Yichen was inspired and sent the ball out diagonally. After a maneuver, Xiao Kaositan's ambition did not die, and he tried to advance again, but he was intercepted by Yichen. Qiu Ting's shot did not find a chance, and Xiao Kaositan revived, kicking a high ball in a good position. Fortunately, Lu Dage caught it correctly and avoided a disaster. The Portuguese army then advanced from the center. Seeing the situation was not good, Zhong En ran out to rescue and kicked the ball out not far. At this time, the rear was empty, and enemy riders trampled on it again. Fortunately, Shang Quan came out from behind and forced a corner kick. Xiao Kaositan was the kicker and was about to show his courage when the time for the first half ended. Donghua took the lead with a score of 2-0.

Donghua Team Continues to Hold the Scoto Cup; Many Good Chances, but Unfortunately They Did Not Succeed 144

You Liang had a good chance at 30 yards out with a high shot, but it was just a little short. At this time, the battle situation was extremely dull. Donghua had many good opportunities, but they all turned out to be empty promises. Sun Jinshun advanced to the goal but was blocked and passed to the back. Economic Special

Stabilizing the Bond Market and Controlling Foreign Exchange 166

— Yu Xiong

Recently, the Ministry of Finance has been implementing a policy of swapping public bonds. This policy is one of the meanings of last year's monetary reform and cannot be criticized in terms of meaning, as it is not based on public power. The main point of this bond swap is to completely unify all types of public bonds. In addition to unifying all public bonds in October, the Ministry also issued 340 million yuan of Reconstruction Public Bonds. Therefore, the amount of public bonds has increased sharply from 160 million yuan to 180 million yuan. The characteristic of the public bond market in the future is that public bonds are completely identical, with only slight differences in repayment periods. Since public bonds are unified and the guarantees and interest rates are equal, speculation and manipulation will be more difficult than before, so speculative practices are expected to be less prevalent than before. However, due to the complete unification of public bonds, the market prices will likely rise and fall in unison. Therefore, future fluctuations in public bond market prices will be spectacular. In the past, public bonds had different repayment periods, slightly different interest rates, and different guarantees, so market prices rose and fell at different times. Even if there were storms, they would not cause a complete disaster. Now that public bonds have been unified, market prices rise and fall completely in unison, and an unusual force is needed to stop them from rising or falling. The current amount of public bonds has reached 180 million, which is actually the largest investment in society. If the public bond market price cannot be kept stable, the financial market will be in turmoil for a long time. Therefore, how to stabilize the public bond market price is the most worthwhile issue to consider.

According to the Ministry of Finance, part of the 200 million yuan of Reconstruction Public Bonds will be allocated to the market stabilization fund. The importance of maintaining the bond market is already in the plans of the authorities. We believe that the authorities may form a bond market stabilization committee to manage this. As for how to stabilize the bond market, the method must come from the common practice of purchasing public bonds when public bond prices fall, reducing the amount of public bonds circulating in the market, and stabilizing the market. When the public bond market price soars and speculation is excessive, public bonds are sold to prevent the market price from rising too high. This mechanical operation is actually what is called open market activity in various countries. If this function can be gradually developed, not only can the public bond market price be more stable, but also the prosperity of market financing can be adjusted. However, in our country at present, there are still some aspects that can be studied.

If a bank purchases public bonds, the other aspect is that the issuance of banknotes will increase, which is inevitable. However, the fluctuation of public bond market prices in our country is more affected by changes in the situation than by changes in the economy. It can be said that public bonds will rise and fall wildly when drastic changes occur in the domestic and foreign political situation. If public bonds rise and fall greatly,

If banks come out and make every effort to stabilize the bond market, with the current amount of debt already reaching 180 million, a large purchase is needed to maintain it. On the other hand, the issuance of banknotes by banks will suddenly expand in a short period of time, which will not only increase public panic, but also make bond market stability more difficult, and the foreign exchange rate may also face a crisis. When the situation changes and public bonds fall in price, it is also the time when funds most want to choose a way to escape. At this juncture, if banks increase the issuance of banknotes to accept public bonds, the general public will simply sell the public bonds to banks to obtain banknotes, and then turn around and purchase foreign exchange, so the foreign exchange will also face a crisis of fluctuation. At least part of the bank's foreign exchange reserves will be lost, which will weaken the bank's ability to stabilize foreign exchange. The result is that even if the public bonds are saved, the exchange rate will not be saved. This situation, especially when the international situation may deteriorate at any time, should be given special attention. If there is no effective remedy, then saving public bonds will be nothing more than a risk for the bank. Moreover, at the critical moment when a crisis occurs, if there is no guarantee method, the bank will not dare to actively stabilize the bond market for the sake of self-protection. The more active the activity, the more mobile funds there will be, and the more people who buy foreign exchange will be. The foreign exchange reserves will decrease more and more. This trend is actually more dangerous than the fall in public bond prices. Therefore, at a critical moment, it is best to make every effort to stabilize foreign exchange.

How to remedy this weakness? This is the center of the problem. The only way, we believe, is to actively prepare to block the road for funds to escape when necessary. Blocking the road for funds to escape will naturally involve the issue of foreign exchange.

Since the monetary reform, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks have been responsible for supplying foreign exchange without restriction. That is, regardless of the motive for a person to purchase foreign exchange, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks are obligated to supply it. That is, the purchase of foreign exchange is completely free and unrestricted. In this way, the Bank of China and other banks have the responsibility to supply foreign exchange without restriction, while the society has the freedom to purchase foreign exchange without restriction. With the limited foreign exchange power of the Bank of China and other banks, supplying the unlimited foreign exchange needs of the entire country, Chinese and foreign, this situation is obviously not easy to maintain. Therefore, we believe that we should actively prepare to control foreign exchange at present, and at least the purchase of foreign exchange should be strictly restricted. We can say with certainty that maintaining stability, because only in this way can we be fearless in actively engaging in the public bond market.

World Silver Market and Chinese Currency 167

— Jiang Yusheng

In June 1934, the United States passed the Silver Purchase Act, turning silver into a political weapon in the global economy. The world silver market entered a new phase, with significant changes in silver prices and the volume of silver flow. The Chinese currency suffered unprecedented misfortune, forcing currency reform. Then, in December 1935, the United States changed its silver purchasing procedures, leading to a sharp drop in silver prices, and the silver market entered its second phase. China's silver flow and monetary system also underwent new international relationships. Now that the global silver tide has come to an end, what position will China's currency be in? This must be answered through practical research on the silver market.

(1) Changes in Silver Prices

After June 1934, the London silver price was completely controlled by the United States. Due to aggressive silver purchases by the United States, coupled with manipulation by London speculators, silver prices soared, from 20 pence per ounce in June to 36 pence per ounce in April 1935. At this time, the United States had become the sole buyer. Realizing that London's manipulation was excessive, it suddenly withdrew from the silver market during the settlement period, causing silver prices to fall rapidly, making it impossible for speculators to gain a foothold for a time. It was not until August 26 that the United States restored the silver price to 29 pence. From August to December 7, the London silver price changed very little, but when calculated against the exchange rate with China at that time, it was still 67% to 27% higher. Therefore, the outflow of Chinese silver did not stop, and international speculators still had active opportunities.

In addition to the above-mentioned London silver price, New York and Mumbai also announced silver prices daily. Before December 1935, the silver prices in the two locations maintained a parallel ratio with London. Before the start of silver purchases, the New York silver price was 45 cents per ounce, equivalent to 20 pence in London. The highest price was 81 cents in April, equivalent to 36 pence in London. After August, it stabilized at 65 cents, equivalent to 29 pence in London. After December 9 last year, New York became an actual trading market, breaking away from the chain of silver prices with London.

During this 18-month silver tide, the difference between the highest and lowest silver prices was the highest record in 15 years. Although the rate of silver price increase was far less than the 89 pence in 1910, the global impact caused by silver price fluctuations, and the use of silver standard countries as speculative tools, was a situation that could not have been imagined 15 years ago.

(2) Silver Flow

After June 1934, the largest buyer of silver - almost the only buyer - was the United States. The main supply of silver was in the East, and the transaction and concentration of silver had always been in London. Therefore, to study the world silver flow during this period, we only need to look at London's statistics to get a glimpse of the whole picture.

The scale of silver flow during this period was unprecedented. Before 1934, the highest was in 1932, when London's total import and export volume was 190 million ounces. However, only half a year after the implementation of the US Silver Purchase Act in 1934, the total amount increased to 282 million ounces, and in 1935 it increased to 685 million ounces. The following statistical table can indicate the direction of silver flow in 1935:

1935 London Silver Flow Table

(Unit: 100 Ounces)

Transcribed from Messrs Mocatta & Goldsmid Annual Circular. The total import and export volume in the table is slightly less than the aforementioned 685 million ounces.

It is worth noting here that the United States was the largest silver buyer in 1935, and Japan and Hong Kong were the largest suppliers. It is found that Japan's annual silver production is only 7 million ounces, while its export volume exceeds its production by more than ten times. Hong Kong is a transit port, and there is no silver production to speak of. Where did their huge amounts of silver come from? Therefore, to study the truth about China's silver outflow during the panic period, we must refer to London's silver flow statistics.

In this environment, China's silver reserves decreased rapidly. According to statistics from Shanghai, the Shanghai silver reserves at the end of June 1934 were 58.2 million yuan, which was reduced to 33.4 million yuan before the currency reform, eventually becoming a major reason for our country's currency reform.

(3) China's Currency Reform and the World Silver Market

China was stimulated by the world silver tide, its finances were depleted, and industry and commerce declined. The government then announced a new monetary system on November 4, centralizing silver reserves, unifying issuance, suspending cash redemption, and stipulating that the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Central Bank would buy and sell foreign exchange without restriction to stabilize exchange rates. This news immediately affected the London silver market that day. Speculators expected that China would centralize silver reserves and that the world silver market would lack silver supply. The silver price rose from 19.3 pence to 19.5 pence. However, this expectation was soon clarified. China's silver supply continued, and stabilizing foreign exchange required exchanging silver. The silver price returned to its original state the next day. According to the British Economic Weekly, China later used high silver prices to sell silver in London. The silver price that previously disrupted China's finances now helped China's foreign exchange reserves. It was not until the United States changed its silver purchasing procedures that China changed its silver transport to New York. It must be stated incidentally that China's silver sales in London are not found in London's statistics. This requires further research.

Following China, Hong Kong reformed its currency system on November 9, issuing orders to ban silver exports and manage foreign exchange, but this was already expected in the London silver market, so it had no significant impact.

(4) The United States Changes Silver Purchasing Procedures

The United States initially launched its silver policy with resounding slogans: first, to increase the purchasing power of Eastern countries; second, to restore the silver standard monetary system for more than half of the world's population; and third, more profoundly and not openly proclaimed, to use it as a weapon of monetary warfare and establish the bimetallic system that the United States had long sought. By December 1935, these goals had tragically failed one by one. The 18-month silver tide forced China, Mexico, and Hong Kong to reform their currency systems, and reduced silver circulation in Italy, Spain, Australia, Peru, and other countries. Except for the United States and Abyssinia, the silver standard monetary system for more than half of the world's population no longer existed.

The silver policy effectively broke the monetary systems of weak countries, and conversely gave the enemies of the United States' monetary warfare opportunities to exploit. The influence of the pound sterling expanded, Japan gained unexpected benefits, and launched the North China Incident. The United States merely hoarded 775 million ounces of silver at a high price of 442 million US dollars, which was still very far from the originally planned gold-silver ratio of 3:1, let alone the gold-silver ratio of 16:1. At this point, the United States had to consider the serious situation at home and abroad, and changed its silver purchasing procedures. Starting from December 9, it gradually reduced the amount of silver purchased in London and switched to purchasing directly from silver-using countries and silver-producing countries. The silver price plummeted as a result. The London price fell from 29 pence on December 7 to 22 pence at the end of the month; the New York price fell from 65 cents on December 9 to 49 cents at the end of the month; the Mumbai price fell from 65 rupees on December 9 to 53 rupees at the end of the month. The world silver market was temporarily plunged into chaos, with London being the worst hit.

Initially, some people speculated that this move by the United States was a precursor to a change in monetary policy, and that the world's currencies would be plunged into even greater turmoil. In reality, it was only a shift from offense to defense by the United States, aimed at salvaging past failures and delivering a fierce blow to speculators. After this sharp drop in silver prices, China can reduce its silver outflows and at the same time change the direction of silver movement.

(5) The Current Situation of the World Silver Market

After the United States changed its silver purchasing procedures, the silver market entered its second stage. The New York silver market has surpassed London's. Silver from China, Mexico, and India is mostly shipped directly to New York. From December 9 of last year to February 14 of this year, the value of silver imported into the United States was more than 70 million US dollars, of which the value of silver purchased from London was more than 7 million pounds, equivalent to more than 30 million US dollars (it is impossible to accurately convert the price for a while), and the value of silver from China was 14.5 million US dollars. At the same time, the flow of silver in the London silver market decreased due to the reduction in silver purchases by the United States, as shown in the following table:

London Silver Flow Table Before and After the United States Changed Its Silver Purchasing Procedures Unit: Thousand Pounds

Compiled according to the British Economic Weekly

After carefully reviewing the above table, the state of silver flow before and after this action can be clearly understood. The first point to note here is that the input of silver in London after the change did not decrease, but the output decreased. One reason is that the silver volume transported to the United States declined; the second point is that the silver volume transported from Japan to London also gradually decreased, which was even more serious in the last two weeks. Hong Kong has a special relationship with the United Kingdom, so it increased instead. In short, the influence of the London silver market has gradually weakened, but London's qualification as an important world silver market will not be lost.

Turning from the flow of silver to the review of silver prices, after the change in the silver market, the silver prices in New York and London broke away from the chain relationship. New York directly posted prices without waiting for telegrams from London, while Mumbai roughly followed the silver prices in London. The most recent silver prices in the two places (according to Reuters) are listed below:
